CHAPTER 6
LITTERING
SECTION:
4-6-1: Definitions
4-6-2: Littering Prohibited
4-6-3: Penalty
4-6-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
PRIVATE PREMISES: All property including, but not limited to, vacant land or
any land, buildings or other structures designed or used for residential,
commercial, business, industrial, institutional or religious purposes, together
with any yard, grounds, walk, driveway, fence, porch, steps, vestibule, mailbox
and other structure appurtenant to it, except any public place.
PUBLIC PLACE: Any and all streets, sidewalks, boulevards, alleys or other
public ways, lakes, rivers, watercourses or fountains and any and all public
parks, squares, spaces, grounds and buildings. (Ord. 2001-8, 12-3-2001)
4-6-2: LITTERING PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to place, cause or allow to be thrown, or
dispose of in any manner any litter, garbage, waste or peelings of vegetables
or fruits, rubbish, ashes, cans, bottles, wire, paper, cartons, boxes, parts of
automobiles, tires, debris, furniture, glass, oil, filthy or odoriferous
objects or anything else of an unsightly or unsanitary nature upon any public
place or private premises, unless duly authorized. (Ord. 2001-8, 12-3-2001)
4-6-3: PENALTY:
Any violation of this chapter shall be considered a misdemeanor. (Ord. 2001-8,
12-3-2001)
CHAPTER 7
SMOKING
SECTION:
4-7-1: Prohibited
4-7-2: Smoking Outside Courthouse
4-7-3: County Employees Disciplined
4-7-4: Penalty
4-7-1: PROHIBITED:
No person shall, at any time, smoke any tobacco, tobacco related product,
filler or other plant or weed in any of the following places owned or operated
by the county:
   A.   Inside any county vehicle.
   B.   Inside any county building or facility. (Ord. 2002-8, 11-12-2002)
4-7-2: SMOKING OUTSIDE COURTHOUSE:
No person shall, at any time, smoke any tobacco, tobacco related product,
filler or other plant or weed within twenty feet (20') of the Payette County
courthouse except at the southeast entrance to the courthouse. "NO SMOKING
WITHIN 20 FEET OF COURTHOUSE" signs shall be posted at all other areas. A
"WARNING:   SMOKING PERMITTED" sign shall be posted at the southeast entrance.
(Ord. 2004-6, 7-12-2004)
4-7-3: COUNTY EMPLOYEES DISCIPLINED:
Any county employee violating this chapter shall be subject to appropriate
discipline, including a reprimand, suspension or termination. (Ord. 2004-6, 7-
12-2004)
4-7-4: PENALTY:
It shall be a misdemeanor to violate section
4-7-1 or
4-7-2 of this chapter. (Ord. 2004-6, 7-12-2004)
CHAPTER 8
OPEN BURNING
SECTION:
4-8-1: Purpose
4-8-2: Definitions
4-8-3: Open Burning Prohibited; Exemptions
4-8-4: Prohibited Burning
4-8-5: Enforcement and Penalties
4-8-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this ordinance is to provide for the health and safety of
Payette County citizens, as well as to protect property within Payette County
by preventing dangerous fires pursuant to County authority under Idaho Code
section 31-714. (Ord. 2023-08, 6-12-2023)
4-8-2: DEFINITIONS:
 
          The term “attended” as used under this chapter shall mean actively supervised, and
ATTENDED: responsibly ignited with proper fire management precautions. All flames, embers,
          coals, sparks, or hot spots shall be completely and fully extinguished such that
          they cannot reignite.
OPEN      The burning of any materials wherein the products of combustion are emitted into
BURNING:  the ambient air without passing through a stack, chimney, or spark arrester from
          an enclosed chamber. (Ord. 2023-08, 6-12-2023)
 
4-8-3: OPEN BURNING PROHIBITED; EXEMPTIONS:
Open burning, and fireworks, as defined by Idaho Code title 39 chapter 26, and
any special or aerial fireworks (e.g., “bottle rockets”) as defined by Idaho
Code section 39-2602, shall be prohibited in the County from July 1 through
October 1 or as determined by resolution of county commissioners.
   A.   Exemptions. This chapter shall not apply to open burning that is:
      1.   Authorized for agricultural purposes by the Idaho Department of
Agriculture.
      2.   Ditch banks and fence rows when attended and controlled.
      3.   Authorized pursuant to a permit or license issued by any other
local, State or Federal governmental agency of competent jurisdiction.
      4.   Conducted by any employee, contractor or agent of any local, State
or Federal governmental agency in the course of performance performing of their
official duties or employment.
      5.   Authorized by and in compliance with federal regulations on federal
land.
      6.   Recreational fires, which shall include a defined area, container or
structure designated for the burning of solid fuel, natural gas or propane. The
fire must be contained within a non-combustible barrier consisting of stone,
brick, concrete, metal or similar noncombustible material in such a manner to
prevent the escape of combustible materials and which shall be attended as
defined above.
      7.   Cooking fires which shall include the burning of conventional fuel
materials such as charcoal, natural or propane gas, or wood pellets, to cook
food in a receptacle such as a barbeque grill, or barbeque pit which was
originally designed or manufactured for such a purpose.
      8.   Residential burning in , including the use of burn barrels, in
enclosed receptacles with appropriate spark arrestors or screen.
      9.   Commercial fireworks as permitted by Idaho Code section 39-2605; or
in-season fireworks as permitted by Idaho Code section 39-2606 and/or Payette
County Ordinance 5-3-4. All other uses are prohibited. (Ord. 2023-08, 6-12-
2023)
4-8-4: PROHIBITED BURNING:
The following shall be prohibited from burning at all times:
   A.   Plastics.
   B.   Dead animals or animal waste.
   C.   Materials from vehicles such as junk motor vehicles or parts, tires,
and other rubber material.
   D.   Construction material such as asphaltic materials, tar and petroleum
materials, paints, treated wood, and insulated wire.
   E.   Trade waste, including any waste generated by construction, commercial,
or industrial activity. (Ord. 2023-08, 6-12-2023)
4-8-5: ENFORCEMENT, PENALTIES AND COSTS:
   A.   Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to limit any expense,
penalty, or liability assessed by any other local, State, or Federal
governmental agency.
   B.   The provisions of this chapter may be enforced by the Sheriff and/or
any peace officer of the State of Idaho authorized by the Sheriff. In addition,
the Sheriff and/or any peace officer of the State of Idaho authorized by the
Sheriff, is authorized to extinguish or cause to be extinguished any open fire
ignited or maintained in violation of this chapter.
   C.   Operation Of Other Laws Not Affected: Nothing in this chapter or any
permit shall exempt any person from the operation of or compliance with any
other State, Federal or local law, regulation or ordinance.
   D.   No Liability: Payette County, its officials, employees and agents shall
not be liable for any claim or cause, regardless of the nature thereof, arising
directly or indirectly from the granting or denial of any permit under this
chapter or performance of any official duty hereunder.
   E.   A violation of any of the provisions of this chapter shall be an
infraction upon a first violation, punishable by a fine as set forth for “other
infractions” in the Idaho Infraction Rule 9 (Idaho Infraction Penalty Schedule)
and shall be a misdemeanor upon a subsequent conviction within five (5) years.
Provided, however, a violation of this chapter where property damage to a third
party occurs shall be a misdemeanor. A misdemeanor shall be punishable by
imprisonment in a county jail not exceeding six (6) months, or by a fine not
exceeding one thousand dollars ($1,000), or by both. (Ord. 2023-08, 6-12-2023)

CHAPTER 2
CURFEW
SECTION:
5-2-1: Curfew Established
5-2-2: Exceptions
5-2-3: Encouraging Delinquency Of A Minor
5-2-4: Prima Facie Evidence; Violation
5-2-5: Penalties
5-2-1: CURFEW ESTABLISHED:
   A.   Under Age Sixteen: It shall be unlawful for any person under the age of
sixteen (16) years to be or to remain, and it shall be unlawful for any parent,
guardian or other person having the care and custody of any person under the
age of sixteen (16) years to permit such person to be or to remain, in or upon
any street, alley, public ground, public places or any place open to the public
or exposed to public use within the County, between the hours of eleven o'clock
(11:00) P.M. and five o'clock (5:00) A.M.
   B.   From Age Sixteen To Eighteen: It shall be unlawful for any person from
the age of sixteen (16) years to eighteen (18) years to be or to remain, and it
shall be unlawful for any parent, guardian or other person having the care and
custody of any person between the age of sixteen (16) years to eighteen (18)
years to permit such person to be or to remain, in or upon any street, alley,
public ground, public places or any place open to the public or exposed to
public use within the County, between the hours of twelve o'clock (12:00)
midnight and five o'clock (5:00) A.M. (Ord. 65, 4-30-1990)
5-2-2: EXCEPTIONS:
The provisions of Section
5-2-1 of this Chapter shall not apply to any person who is accompanied by his
parent, guardian or other adult person having the care and custody of him, or
to any person who is in the performance of an errand or duty directed by his
parent, guardian or other adult person having the care and custody of him, nor
to any person who is actually at the time engaged in legitimate employment for
profit. (Ord. 65, 4-30-1990)
5-2-3: ENCOURAGING DELINQUENCY OF A MINOR:
It shall be unlawful for any person by any act or neglect, to encourage, aid or
cause any person under the age of eighteen (18) years to come within the
purview of Sections
5-2-1 and
5-2-2 of this Chapter. (Ord. 65, 4-30-1990)
5-2-4: PRIMA FACIE EVIDENCE; VIOLATION:
   A.   Under Age Sixteen: The presence of a person under the age of sixteen
(16) years in or upon any street, alley, public ground, public places or any
place open to the public or exposed to public use within the County, between
the hours of eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. and five o'clock (5:00) A.M. not being
accompanied by his parents, guardian or one having legal custody of said child
nor being in the performance of an errand or duty directed by his parent,
guardian or other adult person having the care and custody of him, nor being
actually engaged in legitimate employment for profit shall be prima facie
evidence of a violation of this Chapter.
   B.   From Age Sixteen To Eighteen: The presence of a person between the ages
of sixteen (16) years and eighteen (18) years in or upon any street, alley,
public ground, public places or any place open to the public or exposed to
public use within the County, between the hours of twelve o'clock (12:00)
midnight and five o'clock (5:00) A.M. not being accompanied by his parent,
guardian or one having legal custody of said child, or being in the performance
of an errand or duty directed by his parent, guardian or other adult person
having the care and custody of him, nor being actually engaged in legitimate
employment for profit shall be prima facie evidence of a violation of this
Chapter. (Ord. 65, 4-30-1990)
5-2-5: PENALTIES:
Violation of this Chapter by a minor child shall bring said child within the
purview of the Youth Rehabilitation Act of the State, and violation of this
Chapter by an adult shall be punishable as set forth in Section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord. 65, 4-30-1990; 1996 Code)
CHAPTER 3
FIREWORKS
SECTION:
5-3-1: Definitions
5-3-2: Permits Required For Retail Sales
5-3-3: Authorized Dates For Sale And Use
5-3-4: Prohibitions
5-3-5: Penalties
5-3-1: DEFINITIONS:
The definitions adopted by the Idaho legislature in Idaho Code section 39-2602
are hereby adopted. (Ord. Amd. 52, 6-9-1997)
5-3-2: PERMITS REQUIRED FOR RETAIL SALES:
   A.   The county requires a permit for the retail sale of nonaerial common
fireworks, pursuant to Idaho Code section 39-2602.
   B.   An application for permit may be obtained from the county clerk on a
form approved by the board of county commissioners. Said form shall comply with
Idaho Code regarding retail sales of nonaerial fireworks.
   C.   The applicant must provide at the time of the application a bond or
valid certificate of public liability and property- casualty insurance
providing coverage of up to one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) for
personal injury and property damage.
   D.   The county will assess a fee of twenty five dollars ($25.00) for
issuing a permit and will assess an inspection fee in the amount of twenty five
dollars ($25.00). All fees are to be paid to the county clerk's office.
   E.   An inspection by the county sheriff's department will include an on
site inspection of any temporary fireworks facility and/or stand.
   F.   The permit shall be issued if the application is complete and in
compliance with applicable law, shall be valid for twelve (12) months from the
date of issuance and shall be nontransferable.
   G.   The permit required under this section may be revoked if the permittee
violates any provisions of Idaho Code section 39-2601 et seq. A permit
revocation proceeding shall comply with the provisions of chapter 52, title 67,
Idaho Code.
   H.   The applicant shall display the permit in public view at the location
listed on the permit. (Ord. Amd. 52, 6-9-1997)
5-3-3: AUTHORIZED DATES FOR SALE AND USE:
Nonaerial common fireworks may be sold at retail and used beginning at twelve
o'clock (12:00) midnight June 18, and ending at twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight
July 5, and beginning at twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight December 26, and
ending at twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight January 1. (Ord. Amd. 52, 6-9-1997)
5-3-4: PROHIBITIONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person, except in compliance with this chapter,
to:
   A.   Deploy or use any fireworks or nonaerial common fireworks within five
hundred feet (500') of any nonirrigated lands.
   B.   Deploy or use any fireworks, except for nonaerial common fireworks,
within the unincorporated areas of Payette County.
   C.   Deploy or use fireworks or nonaerial common fireworks in any area that
constitutes a severe fire threat based on the vegetative conditions during the
current fire season as determined by the county commission or authority having
jurisdiction, provided that notice of such areas is given in advance. (Ord.
2006-8, 5-30-2006)
5-3-5: PENALTIES:
Any violation of this chapter shall be a misdemeanor punishable by up to a one
thousand dollar ($1,000.00) fine and six (6) months in the Payette County jail,
or both. In addition to, or in lieu of, any criminal charges, the county shall
be allowed to bring an action for abatement. In any such action the county
shall be allowed to recover all fees and costs. (Ord. 2006-8, 5-30-2006)
CHAPTER 4
PUBLIC ASSEMBLIES
SECTION:
5-4-1: Definitions
5-4-2: Permit Required
5-4-3: Permit Application; Fee
5-4-4: Application Approval
5-4-5: Cash Deposit Or Bond; Liability Insurance
5-4-6: Inspection
5-4-7: Location, Hours And Sound Levels Restricted
5-4-8: Alcoholic Beverages
5-4-9: Narcotic And Dangerous Drugs Prohibited
5-4-10: Crowd Limitations
5-4-11: Responsibility; Revocation Of Permit
5-4-12: Exclusion
5-4-13: Hardship
5-4-14: Compliance
5-4-15: Penalty
5-4-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this Chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this Section:
ASSEMBLY: All assemblies of the public gathered either indoors or outdoors.
HEALTH AUTHORITY: Southwest District Health or the Idaho Department of Health
and Welfare, or its successor.
SHERIFF: The Payette County Sheriff, his duly authorized deputies and
representatives. (Ord. 17, 7-26-1971; 1996 Code)
5-4-2: PERMIT REQUIRED:
It shall be unlawful for any person, landowner, or lessor to allow, promote,
conduct, permit or cause to be advertised, an assembly that said person,
landowner or lessor believes or has reason to believe will attract five hundred
(500) or more persons, whether or not a charge or contribution is required for
admission, unless a completed application, in compliance with this Chapter, has
been submitted to the County Clerk for the operation of said assembly. One such
permit shall be required for each assembly. Criminal or civil liability for
failure to comply with the provisions of this Chapter shall rest in all
persons, landowners or lessors who are responsible for obtaining permits under
this Section. (Ord. 17, 7-26-1971)
5-4-3: PERMIT APPLICATION; FEE:
   A.   Fee: No assembly shall be held in the County unless the person,
landowner or lessor sponsoring said entertainment assembly shall first obtain a
permit as hereinafter provided, and shall comply with all regulations herein
provided. The fee for said permit to cover the cost of inspecting facilities
and issuing and administering same prior to the event shall be:
Number Reasonably     Fee
Anticipated To Attend
Number Reasonably     Fee
Anticipated To Attend
500 to 999            $ 50.00
1,000 to 1,499        100.00
1,500 to 1,999        150.00
2,000 to 2,499        200.00
2,500 to 2,999        250.00
3,000 to 3,499        300.00
4,000 or more         350.00
 
   B.   Application:
      1.   Written Application: Written application for each entertainment
assembly permit shall be made to the County Clerk thirty (30) days or more
prior to the first day upon which such assembly is to be or may be held by
filing the same with the County Clerk and shall be signed by the person
organizing and sponsoring said assembly and verified upon oath. No person who
has not reached the age of twenty one (21) years shall be entitled to make
application for a permit or to sponsor an assembly. Each application shall
state the names of all persons organizing, promoting or sponsoring said
assembly; said application shall state the dates, the number of days and the
hours of the day of the assembly; it shall state the location to be utilized
for said assembly; and it shall state that the applicant or applicants will
abide by all rules and regulations of this Chapter and other regulations and
law for the protection of the health, morals and safety of the persons employed
therein, and for the patrons or participants thereof, and for the public. Each
application shall be accompanied by the fingerprints and a three inch by five
inch (3" x 5") photograph of each and every organizer, promoter and sponsor of
said assembly. Said fingerprints and photographs shall be taken by the Sheriff
at the request of the applicant.
      2.   Transfer Or Assignment: Any permit issued as herein provided shall
be kept posted in a conspicuous place upon the premises of said assembly. No
permit shall be transferable or assignable without the consent of the Board of
County Commissioners. In the event that an application for a permit shall be
withdrawn or denied, a rebate or refund of the deposited fee may be allowed by
the Board of County Commissioners. If a request for rebate or refund is made by
an applicant, any affected agency or department may show expenses incurred with
regard to the particular application for permit. The Board of County
Commissioners shall deduct such expenses from the deposited fee and rebate or
refund to the applicant the sum, if any, that may remain. (Ord. 17, 7-26-1971)
5-4-4: APPLICATION APPROVAL:
   A.   Affected Agencies Or Departments: Within five (5) days after the
application for said permit is made, the applicant shall submit a copy of the
application, together with other information as required by this Chapter, to
the appropriate affected agencies or departments as hereinafter enumerated. No
permit shall be issued unless the respective agency or department has approved
as to each condition.
   B.   Physical Facility; Submission Of Plans; Filing Of Approval: When any
type of physical facility is required or subject to approval hereunder,
preliminary approval may be granted based upon specific plans proposed and
submitted by the applicant. All such facilities shall be in existence five (5)
or more days before the event for which an application is submitted and shall
be subject to inspection by the approving agencies or departments. Should the
actual facility or construction fail to meet the standards approved in the
proposed plans, such preliminary approval shall be withdrawn and any and all
permits granted subject to such approval shall be withdrawn. Approval shall be
on forms provided and shall be filed with the County Clerk. (Ord. 17, 7-26-
1971)
   C.   Conditions For Approval:
      1.   Sanitary Facilities: The Health Authority shall have the
responsibility for approving all sanitation and related facilities to ensure
that reasonable minimum standards have been or will be met by the applicant. In
this regard, the application must provide the Health Authority with a sketch
and other detailed information showing the type, number and location or
proposed location of all toilets, washing facilities, water supply facilities,
food preparation and food service facilities. Approval by the Health Authority
shall indicate the number, type and location (when appropriate) of the toilet,
washing and water supply facilities. If food is to be served on the premises,
approval must be given as to the type of food preparation and food service
facilities to be provided. (Ord. 17, 7-26-1971; 1996 Code)
      2.   Fire Protection Standards:
         a.   Proper Approval Required: No permit shall be granted hereunder
unless the applicant has shown that the appropriate fire protection district
officer has approved fire protection devices and equipment available. Such
approval must extend to any building, tent, stadium or enclosure wherein or
whereupon more than ten (10) persons may be expected to congregate at any time
during the course of such assembly for which a permit is hereunder required,
and to potentially flammable material in the area, including but not limited to
trees, grass and brush. If site for which the permit is applied is located
outside a fire protection district, the applicant must show approval from the
Sheriff.
         b.   Motorized Racing Event: Approved minimum fire protection
equipment for any type of motorized racing event shall include three (3) five
(5) pound CO2 fire extinguishers. (Ord. 17, 7-26-1971)
      3.   Medical Services:
         a.   Health Authority Approval Required: The Health Authority shall
have responsibility for approving plans as to medical service required for the
assembly. Each assembly shall have as a minimum one ambulance and a first aid
station staffed by two (2) adult individuals trained in first aid techniques.
(Ord. 17, 7-26-1971; 1996 Code)
         b.   Motorized Racing Event: All motorized racing events must have an
ambulance with attendants present on standby at the start of all races and
during all races and time trials or the race or time trial must stop until the
ambulance and attendants are present.
      4.   Public Safety; Traffic Control And Crowd Protection: The applicant
must submit his plans for public safety at the assembly to the Sheriff for his
approval.
         a.   Personnel Required: Adequate traffic control and crowd protection
policing must have been contracted for or otherwise provided by the applicant.
There shall be provided one traffic- control person for each two hundred fifty
(250) persons expected or reasonably expected to be in attendance at any time
during the event.
         b.   Fitness Of Personnel: The applicant shall submit the names and
necessary background information on forms provided by the Sheriff for all
traffic control and crowd control personnel to be utilized during the assembly
for investigation by the Sheriff as to fitness. All such personnel must meet
the following minimum standards in order to be approved as suitable by the
Sheriff:
            (1)   Be twenty one (21) through sixty five (65) years of age.
            (2)   Be in good physical health.
            (3)   Never have been convicted of a felony or misdemeanor
involving moral turpitude.
            (4)   Either have received reasonable minimum training in law
enforcement or have on-the-job experience in law enforcement.
         c.   Identifying Uniform; Relief Schedule: All policing personnel must
wear an appropriate identifying uniform and must be on duty during the entire
assembly unless a relief schedule has been planned and approved. A relief
schedule will be approved by the Sheriff only when sufficient policing strength
on duty has been maintained to meet the abovedescribed minimum strength
standards.
         d.   Duties: It shall be the duty of policing personnel to report any
violations of the law to the Sheriff, his deputies, or representatives and to
take whatever action as can reasonably be expected of them to enforce the law.
      5.   Parking Facilities: The applicant shall provide the Sheriff with a
scale drawing showing adequate parking facilities have been made available
within or adjacent to the location for which the permit is requested. Such
parking facilities shall provide parking space for one vehicle for every four
(4) persons expected or reasonably to be expected to attend such event.
Adequate ingress and egress shall be provided from such parking area to
facilitate the movement of any vehicle at any time to or from the parking area;
provided, that should buses be used to transport the public to said event it
shall be shown that public parking or parking as described above is available
at any site within the County from which buses are scheduled to pick up persons
to transport them to said event. (Ord. 17, 7-26-1971)
5-4-5: CASH DEPOSIT OR BOND; LIABILITY INSURANCE:
   A.   Indemnification Limits:
      1.   Attendance Less Than Five Thousand: No permit shall be issued
hereunder unless the applicant has on deposit with the County Treasurer the sum
of ten thousand dollars ($10,000.00) cash or bond as an indemnity to save and
protect the streets, pavements, bridges, road signs and other property of the
County from any and all damages that may be caused by vehicles, employees, or
participants in such assembly and to be used, if necessary, to restore the
grounds where such assembly is held to a sanitary condition and pay all charges
and losses to the County for damages to the streets, bridges, and other
property.
      2.   Attendance Over Five Thousand: A twenty five thousand dollar
($25,000.00) bond shall be required if over five thousand (5,000) persons are
reasonably anticipated to attend the assembly.
   B.   Additional Services Required: Should the licensed event require police,
sanitary and/or fire protection services in excess of services customarily
supplied, such added expense shall be recoverable from the principal and its
surety out of the cash on deposit and/or the bond. The deposit or its balance
shall be returned when the Board of County Commissioners certifies to the
Treasurer that no damage has been done and that the County did not incur
additional expenses due to said licensed event or that the cost of the above
has been paid by the permittee.
   C.   Liability Insurance: In addition, the permit applicants shall be
required to furnish evidence of liability insurance providing for a minimum of
one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) bodily injury coverage per person;
three hundred thousand dollars ($300,000.00) bodily injury coverage per
occurrence and one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) property damage
coverage, naming the County as an additional insured. (Ord. 17, 7-26-1971)
5-4-6: INSPECTION:
No application shall be granted hereunder unless the applicant shall in writing
upon the application for such permit consent to allow law enforcement, public
health and fire control officers to come upon the premises for which the permit
has been granted for the purpose of inspection and enforcement of the terms and
conditions thereunder. (Ord. 17, 7-26-1971)
5-4-7: LOCATION, HOURS AND SOUND LEVELS RESTRICTED:
   A.   Location; Hours Of Operation: No assembly shall be conducted in the
unincorporated areas of the County within one thousand feet (1,000') of any
residence between the hours of one minute after twelve o'clock (12:01) midnight
and nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. and in all other areas between the hours of two
o'clock (2:00) A.M. and nine o'clock (9:00) A.M.
   B.   Sound Level: The use of amplified sound shall be regulated in such a
manner that it shall not interfere with normal usage of any school, church,
residence or other permanent place of human habitation unless prior written
consent is obtained from all affected persons. A sound level in excess of
seventy (70) decibels between nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. and ten o'clock (10:00)
P.M. and in excess of fifty (50) decibels between ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and
nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. (as measured upon the A scale of a standard sound
level meter on affected property) shall constitute interference. (Ord. 17, 7-
26-1971)
5-4-8: ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES:
No person conducting an assembly, nor any person having charge or control
thereof at any time when an assembly is being conducted shall permit any person
to bring into said assembly or upon the premises thereof, any alcoholic
beverage, nor permit any alcoholic beverage to be consumed on the premises, and
no person during said time shall take or carry onto said premises or drink
thereon any alcoholic beverage. In accordance with Idaho statutes, this
provision shall not apply to the sale and consumption of alcoholic beverages
from a facility located on the premises of an assembly when licensed by the
State. (Ord. 17, 7-26-1971)
5-4-9: NARCOTIC AND DANGEROUS DRUGS PROHIBITED:
No person conducting an assembly, nor any person having charge or control
thereof at any time when an assembly is being conducted shall permit any person
to bring into said assembly, or upon the premises thereof, any "narcotic" or
"dangerous drug", as defined by Idaho statutes, nor permit narcotic or
dangerous drugs to be used on the premises. (Ord. 17, 7-26-1971)
5-4-10: CROWD LIMITATIONS:
   A.   If at any time during said assembly the size of the crowd exceeds ten
percent (10%) of the number of persons expected to be in attendance, the
Sheriff, or any of his deputies, shall require the permittee or sponsor to
limit further admissions until sanitation, parking, fire, health, traffic,
medical, and crowd control requirements have been brought into conformity with
standards herein.
   B.   All assemblies operating without a permit under the terms of this
Chapter due to the fact that less than five hundred (500) persons were
reasonably anticipated to attend shall limit attendance therein to four hundred
ninety nine (499) persons. (Ord. 17, 7-26-1971; 1996 Code)
5-4-11: OPERATOR RESPONSIBILITY; REVOCATION OF PERMIT:
The burden of preserving order shall be upon the operator of the assembly. Any
permit granted under this Chapter may be revoked at any time without notice or
formal hearing by the Board of County Commissioners an/or the County Sheriff
upon their finding that any police, sanitary or fire rule or regulation set
forth by this Chapter and/or State law has been violated. The revocation of any
permit granted under this Chapter shall not preclude the imposition of further
penalties as provided for in this Chapter and State law. (Ord. 17, 7-26-1971)
5-4-12: EXCLUSION:
This Chapter shall not apply to any regularly organized and supervised school
district activity or program that takes place on school property, nor to any
activity of a municipal corporation or government agency. A permit shall not be
required for nonrecurring assemblies of a duration not greater than one day if
the duration is no longer than eight (8) hours during said day. However, no
person shall conduct or permit an entertainment "assembly" as defined by this
Chapter unless notice in writing of the event is filed with the County Clerk at
least ten (10) days prior to the event. Such notice shall state the time,
place, nature of the event and the names of persons responsible. (Ord. 17, 7-
26-1971)
5-4-13: HARDSHIP:
Should the application of any provision or condition of this Chapter be
determined to be unduly harsh or prove to be an extreme hardship to any
applicant under the circumstances existing at the time an application is made
for a permit hereunder, the Board of County Commissioners may, in the exercise
of its discretion, waive any of the requirements of this Chapter as the same
may apply to said applicant taking into consideration the extreme hardship
which would be created if strict compliance with this Chapter were required.
(Ord. 17, 7-26-1971)
5-4-14: COMPLIANCE:
Compliance with the terms and conditions of this Chapter shall constitute
minimum health, sanitation and safety provisions, and failure to comply with
the terms and conditions of this Chapter and State law shall constitute a
public nuisance and shall be subject to all criminal, civil and equitable
remedies as such. (Ord. 17, 7-26-1971)
5-4-15: PENALTY:
Any person who shall violate or fail to comply with any provision of this
Chapter, or, who, having obtained a permit hereunder, wilfully fails to
continue to comply with the terms and conditions thereunder, or who shall
counsel, aid or abet such a violation or failure to comply shall be deemed
guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be subject to penalty as provided in Section
1-4-1 of this Code. A failure from day to day to comply with this Chapter shall
be a separate offense for each such day. (Ord. 17, 7-26-1971; 1996 Code)
CHAPTER 5
DOGS
SECTION:
5-5-1: Definitions
5-5-2: License Requirements
5-5-3: License Tags
5-5-4: Police Authority
5-5-5: Offenses And Conditions
5-5-6: Harboring Of Dangerous Dogs
5-5-7: Guard Dogs Excepted
5-5-8: Keeping Guard Dogs
5-5-9: Insurance
5-5-10: Identification Photographs
5-5-11: Pit Bulls Prohibited (Rep. by Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-12: Responsibility
5-5-13: Action For Damages
5-5-14: Restrictions (Rep. by Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-15: Impoundment Procedures
5-5-16: Disposition Of Unclaimed Dogs
5-5-17: Owners To Pay Costs
5-5-18: Procedure For Declaring A Dog Dangerous
5-5-19: Penalties
5-5-1: DEFINITIONS:
CONFINED: Keeping an animal within an enclosure that cannot be readily or
easily opened by any person other than the owner or with the owner's assistance
or consent and from which an animal cannot escape.
   A.   A dangerous dog is "confined" as the term is used in this chapter if
such dog is securely confined indoors or confined in a securely enclosed and
locked pen or structure upon the premises of the person in possession of such
dog in a manner described in this chapter. At a minimum, such pen or structure
must have secure sides and a secure top. If the pen or structure has no bottom
secured to the sides, the sides must be embedded in the ground no less than two
feet (2') (0.6096 m). Said pen or structure shall be sufficiently secured with
redundant locking mechanisms to prevent unauthorized persons from releasing the
enclosed animal. Said pen shall also be sufficiently secure to keep the animal
from releasing itself. A list of approved building materials for such
structures will be maintained by the sheriff and made available upon request.
All such structures shall be constructed in such a manner, and of such
materials, as approved by the county building inspector and the sheriff or his
appointed representative. A certificate of inspection of the structures shall
be made a part of that dog's file at the Payette County sheriff's office.
   B.   A dangerous dog is "unconfined" as the term is used in this chapter if
such dog is not securely confined indoors or confined in a securely enclosed
and locked pen or structure upon the premises of the person in possession of
such dog as defined in this chapter. At a minimum, a pen or structure must have
secure sides and a secure top. If the pen or structure has no bottom secured to
the sides, the sides must be embedded in the ground no less than two feet (2')
(0.6096 m). Said pen or structure shall be sufficiently secure to keep
unauthorized persons from readily or easily releasing the enclosed animal. Said
pen shall also be sufficiently secure to keep the animal from releasing itself.
A list of approved building materials for such structures will be maintained by
the sheriff and made available upon request. All such structures shall be
constructed in such a manner, and of such materials, as approved by the county
building inspector and/or the sheriff or his appointed representative. A
certificate of inspection of the structures shall be made a part of that dog's
file at the Payette County sheriff's office.
DANGEROUS DOG: A. Any of the following, only one of which is required to
declare a dog dangerous:
   1.   Any dog that makes an unprovoked attack that causes bodily injury to a
human being and the attack occurs off the owner's premises. "Bodily injury"
means lacerations, broken bones, punctures of the skin, or any physical injury
resulting in death;
   2.    A dog that has bitten, attacked, approached in a dangerous, vicious,
or terrorizing manner or otherwise endangered livestock without provocation and
the event occurs off the owner's premises;
   3.   A dog that, without intentional provocation, has chased or approached a
person on the streets, sidewalks, or any public place in a menacing, vicious,
or terrorizing manner or with an apparent attitude of attack, whether or not
the attack is consummated or is capable of being consummated;
   4.   A dog that bites or attacks and causes serious injury or death to
another dog while the other dog is on the owner's property or under the dog
owner's control;
   5.   Any dog, which on private property, when unprovoked, in a vicious or
terrifying manner approaches in an apparent attitude of attack, or bites, or
inflicts injury, or otherwise attacks a mailman, meter reader, serviceman,
delivery man, or other person who is on the dog owner's property with
permission;
   6.   Any dog which, whether on public or private property, in a vicious or
terrifying manner approaches in an apparent attitude of attack, or bites, or
inflicts injury, or otherwise attacks the sheriff, a deputy sheriff, police
officer, ordinance or animal control officer or agent, or other county employee
in the performance of their duties; or
   7.   Any dog, which is bred, trained, owned, possessed, or kept for the
purpose of dogfighting.
   B.   The term "dangerous dog" shall not apply to the following:
   1.    Any dog used by the sheriff or police for law enforcement purposes.
   2.   Any dog on the owner's premises causing injury to a person committing a
trespass or other tort, or causing injury to a person committing or attempting
to commit a crime at the time of the injury, or causing injury to one who is
teasing, tormenting or assaulting the dog in a manner that an ordinary and
reasonable person would conclude was intentionally antagonizing the dog.
GUARD DOG: Any dog trained or used to protect persons or property by attacking
or threatening to attack any person found within the area patrolled by the dog
and that is either securely enclosed within that area at all times or under the
continuous control of a trained handler.
ORDINANCE OFFICER: That person employed or assigned by the Payette County
sheriff's office who has as their primary responsibility the enforcement of all
county ordinances including all animal control ordinances.
OWNER: Any person who owns, possesses, keeps, exercises control over,
maintains, harbors, feeds, waters, transports, or sells a dog or one who
assists another in possession, sale, transport, harboring, feeding, watering or
maintenance thereof. An owner need not have any pecuniary, proprietary or
economic interest in a dog.
SECURE TEMPORARY ENCLOSURE: A secure enclosure used for purposes of
transporting a dog and which includes a top and bottom permanently attached to
the sides except for a door for removal of the animal. Such enclosure shall be
of such material and of such construction that when the door is closed the dog
cannot exit the enclosure on its own. (Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-2: LICENSE REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   License Required: It shall be unlawful for any person to own or keep a
dangerous dog within Payette County prior to the issuance of a county of
Payette dog license. No license shall be issued to the owner of any dangerous
dog prior to complete compliance with all sections of this chapter. Compliance
with this chapter shall be verified by the sheriff, or his designee.
   B.   Dangerous Dog Annual License Fees:
      1.   The Payette County clerk, or a designee, is hereby authorized to
issue a license to any person who presents a completed dangerous dog license
application along with veterinary certification of rabies vaccination,
compliance with all requirements of this chapter, and upon payment of one
hundred dollars ($100.00) per head for each dangerous dog. A list of specific
dogs, which have been declared or adjudicated as dangerous, will be maintained
by the Payette County sheriff and such list will be provided to the Payette
County clerk's office. Owners presenting veterinary certification that the
dangerous dog has been spayed or neutered will pay seventy five dollars
($75.00) per head. All licenses issued will be valid from the date of issue and
will expire on December 31 of each year.
      2.   The owner of a dangerous dog shall keep the current license for such
dangerous dog through annual renewal. Such license is not transferable and
shall be renewable only by the holder of the license or by a member of the
immediate family of such licensee. A special license tag of such color and
design that will allow clear and easy visual identification of the animal as a
dangerous dog will be issued to the owner at the time the dangerous dog license
is issued. This tag shall be worn at all times by the dog.
   C.   Due Date: Such license fees shall be due and payable on January 1 of
each year, except as hereinafter provided.
   D.   Penalty And Exceptions: If any license fee is not paid on or before
January 31 of each year, the Payette County clerk shall collect a penalty in
addition to said license fee in the sum of ten dollars ($10.00); provided,
however, that any dog born subsequent to January 31 of any year shall be
licensed by the payment of the appropriate license fee, without penalty, within
four (4) months after its birth, and thereafter the penalty shall be added as
hereinbefore set forth, and any dog brought into the county subsequent to
January 31 of any year shall be licensed by the payment of the appropriate
license fee, without penalty, within thirty (30) days after being brought into
the county, and thereafter the penalty shall be added as hereinbefore set
forth. (Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-3: LICENSE TAGS:
   A.   Tag To Be Worn: Every owner shall be required to provide each dangerous
dog a collar or harness to which the license tag must be securely affixed, and
shall ensure that the collar and the tag are constantly worn. Show dogs, during
showing, are exempted from wearing the collar and tag.
   B.   Lost Tag: Replacement dangerous dog license tags shall be issued by the
county clerk upon certification that the original tag was lost or destroyed and
upon payment of ten dollars ($10.00) for each such replaced tag.
   C.   Unlawful To Remove: No person shall remove or cause to be removed the
collar or tag from any licensed dog without consent of the owner, keeper or
harborer thereof. (Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-4: POLICE AUTHORITY:
   A.   Fresh Pursuit: In the enforcement of any provision of this chapter, any
sheriff, sheriff's deputy, peace officer, police officer, ordinance officer or
other public officer, is authorized to enter the premises of any person to take
possession of licensed or unlicensed roaming, fierce, or dangerous dogs when in
pursuit of any such dog at the time the dog goes onto private property.
   B.   Exhibit License: It shall be unlawful for any owner or person keeping
or harboring a dog for which a license is required by this chapter to fail or
refuse to exhibit the license or tag upon demand by a sheriff, sheriff's
deputy, police officer, ordinance officer, or other designated county official.
   C.   Interference With Police: Any person who shall molest, interrupt,
hinder or prevent the sheriff, or any peace officer, ordinance officer, or
other public officer, in the discharge of his duty herein prescribed, shall be
guilty of a misdemeanor.
   D.   Authority To Enter Premises: In the enforcement of any provision of
this chapter, any sheriff, deputy sheriff, ordinance officer, or other public
officer, is authorized to enter the premises of any person to take possession
of any unlicensed or licensed, roaming, or dangerous dogs, whether or not in
pursuit of any such dog, if the dog is in plain view of the officer from a
public area. (Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-5: OFFENSES AND CONDITIONS:
   A.   Running At Large Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any "owner" as
defined in section 5-5-1 of this chapter, to permit a dog to be, remain, or run
at large, off or away from the premises of the owner, possessor, or keeper
thereof, unless: 1) upon the private premises of another with the consent of
the person in possession of such premises; or 2) such dog be under the direct
and immediate care and control of a person and controlled by a leash not
exceeding fifteen feet (15') in length; or 3) such dog(s) trained for hunting
and are being legitimately operated while off leash on private or public lands
as hunting dogs and such dogs are under the supervision of a licensed hunter
(so long as such dogs have not been declared dangerous dogs); or 4) such dogs
be safely confined in a motor vehicle. No dog shall be left inside a vehicle
when the temperature and/or humidity are high or when temperatures are near or
below freezing. Dogs secured in the bed of a pickup or cargo area of any truck
must be secured in such a manner as to prevent any part of their body from
extending past the edge of the platform or bed, to the extent the pickup or
truck is parked in parking area open to the public.
   B.   Impoundment: Any dog found running at large may be immediately seized,
captured or taken up and impounded and such dog may be so taken without the
necessity of filing a complaint. Such dog shall be impounded and disposed of in
accordance with provisions in this chapter.
   C.   Disturbances: It shall be unlawful for any "owner" as defined in this
chapter, to keep any dog within the county limits which by loud, continuous,
frequent, or habitual barking, howling, whining, or yelping, annoys or disturbs
any neighborhood or person. Any dog, which has persistently created the noises
referred to in this subsection, as demonstrated by two (2) or more convictions
of the owner thereof for violating this subsection, is declared to be a public
nuisance and may be impounded.
   D.   Sanitary Conditions: Every person who shall keep, maintain or harbor a
dog shall maintain his premises, including, but not limited to, dog pens or
runs, in a clean and sanitary condition so that they shall not be offensive, a
harborage for vermin, or a health hazard.
   E.   Inspection: Whenever any person applies for and is granted a license to
maintain a dangerous dog, the application is permission from the applicant for
the sheriff, or his designee, to make whatever inquiry is deemed necessary,
including, but not limited to, entry onto the applicant's property to ensure
ongoing compliance with all provisions of this chapter. Any entry shall be
limited to the purpose of compliance inspections of the licensed premises and
the licensed animal, and will be made in the presence of the owner whenever
practical. (Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-6: HARBORING OF DANGEROUS DOGS:
   A.   Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any person to keep or harbor a
fierce or dangerous animal or dog without first complying with the terms of
this chapter. It shall be an affirmative defense to charges under this section
if the actual or intended victim of any attack has made an unlawful entry into
the dwelling of the owner.
   B.   Dangerous Dog Unconfined: No "owner", as defined in this chapter, of a
dangerous dog shall suffer or permit such animal to go unconfined on the
premises of such person.
   C.   Dangerous Dog Leashed And Muzzled: No "owner", as defined in this
chapter, shall suffer or permit such dog to go beyond the premises of such
person unless such dog is securely leashed and muzzled. When on leash, the
leash shall consist of a short high tensile strength material with a maximum
length of three feet (3') (0.9144 m). A dangerous dog shall not be required to
be muzzled when shown either in a sanctioned American Kennel Club or United
Kennel Club show. (Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-7: GUARD DOGS EXCEPTED:
Dogs maintained as guard dogs, as defined in section 5-5-1 of this chapter and
in compliance with this chapter shall not be included under this. (Ord. 2017-1,
1-23-2017)
5-5-8: KEEPING GUARD DOGS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to place or maintain guard dogs in any area
for the protection of persons or property unless the following provisions are
met:
   A.   The dogs shall be confined to an enclosed area adequate to ensure they
will not escape; or
   B.   They shall be under the absolute control of a handler at all times when
not securely enclosed; and
   C.   In either instance of subsection A or B of this section, the owner or
other persons in control of the premises upon which a guard dog is maintained
shall post warning signs on, over or next to all exterior doors stating that
such dog is on the premises. At least one such sign shall be posted at each
driveway or entranceway to said premises. Such signs shall be in lettering
clearly visible from either the curb line or a distance of fifty feet (50'),
whichever is less, and shall contain a telephone number where some person
responsible for controlling such guard dog can be reached twenty four (24)
hours a day; and
   D.   Prior to the placing of a guard dog on any property, the person or
persons responsible for the placing shall inform the sheriff, ordinance
officer, the fire department and any utilities who have personnel that come
upon premises or any business that is invited to come or send employees upon
the premises, in writing, of their intention to post said dog or dogs, the
number of dogs to be posted, the location where said dog or dogs will be
posted, the approximate length of time said dog or dogs will be guarding the
area, the daily hours said dog or dogs will be guarding the area, the breed,
sex, age and rabies tag number of said dog or dogs. Such notice must be renewed
every six (6) months. (Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-9: INSURANCE:
All owners of dangerous dogs as defined in this chapter shall, within ten (10)
days of the effective date of this section, provide proof to the Payette County
clerk of public liability insurance in a single incident amount of no less than
one million dollars ($1,000,000.00) for bodily injury to or death of any person
or persons or for damage to property owned by any persons which may result from
the ownership, keeping or maintenance of such animal. This policy shall include
the county of Payette as an additional named insured, with minimum limits of
coverage of one million dollars ($1,000,000.00), and shall have the effect of
saving harmless and defending the county of Payette and its officers, agents
and employees from all suits, claims, demands or actions at law or in equity
arising directly or indirectly as the result of injury to persons or damage to
property occasioned by the maintenance of the dangerous dog by the owner. The
policy shall contain a provision requiring the insurance company to provide
written notice to the sheriff not less than fifteen (15) days prior to any
cancellation, termination, or expiration of the policy. (Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-
2017)
5-5-10: IDENTIFICATION PHOTOGRAPHS:
All owners, keepers or harborers of dangerous dogs must within ten (10) days of
the effective date of this section provide to the county clerk two (2) color
photographs of the registered animal clearly showing the color and approximate
size of the animal. (Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-11: PIT BULLS PROHIBITED:
(Rep. by Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-12: RESPONSIBILITY:
Owners of dogs shall be liable for any damage done by their dogs to any person,
domestic animal, livestock, or property, or for any costs incident to taking up
and keeping their dog. Additionally, the owners of any dog which shall bite any
person while such person is on or in a private place, including the property of
the owner, shall be liable for such damages as may be suffered by persons
bitten, regardless of the former dangerousness of such dog or the owner's
knowledge of such dangerousness.
A person is lawfully upon private property of such owner within the meaning of
this chapter when he or she is on such property in the performance of any duty
imposed upon him by the laws of this state or by the laws of postal regulations
of the United States, or when he or she is on such property upon invitation,
expressed or implied, of the owner thereof; or when he or she is on such
property in the performance of a duty relative to public safety, which shall
include policemen, firemen, or other authorized members of boards or agencies
of county government; provided, however, no owner of any dog shall be liable
for any damages to any person or his property when such person shall
mischievously or carelessly provoke or aggravate the dog inflicting such
damage. (Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-13: ACTION FOR DAMAGES:
If any dangerous animal shall, when unprovoked, kill or wound, or assist in
killing or wounding any sheep, goat, lamb, cattle, horse, hog, swine, fowl, or
other domestic animal, belonging to or in the possession of any person, or
shall, when unprovoked, attack, assault, bite or otherwise injure any human
being or assist in attacking, assaulting, biting or otherwise injuring any
human being while out of or within the enclosure of the owner or keeper of such
dangerous animal, or while otherwise, on or off the property of the owner
whether or not such dangerous animal was on a leash and securely muzzled or
whether the dangerous animal escaped without fault of the owner or keeper, the
owner or keeper of such animal shall be liable to the person aggrieved as
aforesaid, for all damage sustained, to be recovered in a civil action, with
costs of suit. It is rebuttably presumed as a matter of law that the owning,
keeping or harboring of a dangerous animal in violation of this chapter is a
nuisance. It shall not be necessary, in order to sustain any such action, to
prove that the owner of such dangerous animal knew that such dangerous animal
possessed the propensity to cause such damage or that the dangerous animal had
a dangerous nature. Upon such attack or assault, the sheriff or his designee is
hereby empowered to confiscate and destroy such dangerous animal, if the
conduct of such dangerous animal or its owner constituted a violation of the
provisions of this chapter, punishable by the confiscation and destruction of
the animal. (Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-14: RESTRICTIONS:
(Rep. by Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-15: IMPOUNDMENT PROCEDURES:
   A.   Impounding: The sheriff, his designee, or other animal control officer
having probable cause to believe that any person has violated any provision of
this chapter for which an animal may be impounded including, but not limited
to, a determination that a dog is dangerous, may impound such an animal;
provided, however, that if any dog so found at large or determined to be
dangerous that cannot be safely taken up and impounded, such dog may be
destroyed forthwith if the officer determines that the dog poses a threat to
public safety. If a dog is found to be in need of shelter or care when an owner
is arrested or detained, the dog shall be impounded. Any action taken by a
sheriff, sheriff's deputy, police officer, ordinance officer or other
designated county employee, in the performance of his duties, that requires the
death, injury or destruction of a dangerous dog or dangerous dog found running
at large, shall not be considered to be cruel or inhumane treatment of the
animal.
   B.   Biting Dogs Or Dogs With Rabies: Any dog which bites any person and
causes a break in the skin of that person, regardless if the bite is provoked
or unprovoked, or is suspected of having rabies, shall be seized and impounded
for a period of ten (10) days as required by state law. The sheriff and health
department shall be so notified and the animal disposed of only under their
direction. A complete registry shall be kept of every dog so impounded,
entering the breed, color and sex of such dog, whether licensed, and time and
place of taking. If licensed, the name and address of the owner and the number
of the license tag shall be entered.
   C.   Impoundment Fees:
      1.   Any person who owns, possesses, keeps, is in charge of the care of
or who is responsible for a dog, shall be liable for all impound and quarantine
fees provided for in this chapter. The impound or quarantine fees for any dog
which is impounded for running at large, for biting, for being suspected of
being infected with rabies, or for any other reason shall be as follows: for
the first occurrence of impounding or quarantining a dog, the responsible party
thereof shall pay to the county a fee of fifty dollars ($50.00) for the taking
up of such animal; for the second occurrence of impounding or quarantining a
dog, the responsible party thereof shall pay to the county a fee of seventy
five dollars ($75.00) for the taking up of such animal; for the third or any
subsequent occurrence of impounding or quarantining a dog, the responsible
party thereof shall pay the county a fee of one hundred dollars ($100.00) for
the taking up of such animal for each such occurrence. Said fees shall be paid
to the sheriff's office and are in addition to any fines or restitution ordered
by the court. In addition to the fees set forth above, in the event a dog is
impounded or quarantined for biting or being suspected of having rabies, a fee
of ten dollars ($10.00) per day shall be paid for each day the dog is in the
possession of the county.
   D.   Care Of Impounded Animals: Any animal impounded under the provisions of
this chapter shall be provided with proper care, food and water while so
confined.
   E.   Additional Fees For Care: All dogs impounded and held for more than
three (3) days as required by state law, or this chapter, will require the
owner to pay a ten dollar ($10.00) fee per day for each twenty four (24) hour
period, or portion thereof, that the dog is impounded. (Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-16: DISPOSITION OF UNCLAIMED DOGS:
All dogs impounded shall be kept for a maximum period of three (3) days. If
possession of any dog is not recovered as above set forth, the dog may be
disposed of by delivery to any person who will pay the license fee and costs
herein provided, by delivery to a third party humane shelter, or the dog may be
destroyed in a humane manner. (Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-17: OWNERS TO PAY COSTS:
The owner or representative of the owner of any dog which may be taken up and
impounded under the provisions of this chapter, may recover possession of such
dog upon payment to the county the impoundment fees, and other costs herein
provided together with payment to the appropriate animal shelter, if any,
unless such dog is of a prohibited class of dog or subject to a court order to
the contrary. (Ord. 2017-1, 1-23-2017)
5-5-18: PROCEDURE FOR DECLARING A DOG DANGEROUS:
   A.   Declaration Of Dangerous: The animal control officer or sheriff, or his
designee may find and declare a dog dangerous if he has probable cause to
believe the animal falls within the definition as set forth in this chapter.
The finding shall be based upon:
      1.   A written complaint of a citizen who is willing to testify that the
animal has acted in a manner which causes such animal to fall within the
definition of a "dangerous dog"; or
      2.   Actions of the dog witnessed by any law enforcement officer; or
      3.   Other substantial evidence admissible in court under the Idaho rules
of evidence.
   B.   Exceptions:
      1.   No dog may be declared to be a dangerous dog when at the time of the
dangerous behavior, the precipitating cause constituted justified provocation.
Justified provocation includes, but is not limited to, the following:
         a.   The dog was protecting or defending a person within the immediate
vicinity of the dog from an attack or assault;
         b.   The person was committing a crime or offense upon the property of
the owner or custodian of the dog;
         c.   The person was at the time, or had in the past, wilfully
tormented, abused or assaulted the dog;
         d.   The dog was responding to pain or injury or protecting its
offspring;
         e.   The dog was working as a hunting dog, herding dog or predator
control dog on the property of, or under the control of, its owner or keeper,
and the damage or injury sustained was to a person who was interfering with the
dog while the dog was working in a place where it was lawfully engaged in such
activity, including public lands;
         f.   The dog was a service animal individually trained to do work or
perform tasks for a person with a disability; or
         g.   The person was intervening between two (2) or more animals
engaged in aggressive behavior or fighting.
      2.   The burden of proof on establishing that the dog falls into one of
the exceptions described in subsection B1 of this section is on the owner/
possessor of the dog.
   C.   Determination: At the conclusion of the investigation, the sheriff may:
      1.   Determine that the dog is not dangerous and, if the dog is
impounded, may waive any impoundment fees incurred and, afterward, release the
dog to its owner; or
      2.   Determine that the dog is dangerous and order the owner to comply
with all requirements of this chapter for keeping a dangerous dog, and if the
dog is impounded, release the dog to its owner only after the owner has paid
all fees incurred for the impoundment and licensing of the dog. Fees must be
paid within ten (10) days after final determination that the dog is dangerous
or the sheriff may cause the dog to be humanely destroyed; or
      3.   Determine that the dog is dangerous and order the destruction of the
dog pursuant to this chapter.
   D.   Notification Of Dangerous Dog Declaration: Within five (5) business
days after declaring a dog dangerous, the sheriff or his designee shall serve
written notice on the owner or possessor of the dog of its designation as a
dangerous dog in one of the following methods:
      1.   Certified mail to the owner's or possessor's last known address, if
known; or
      2.   Personally served to the owner or to another person eighteen (18)
years of age or older and mentally competent residing at the owner or
possessor's residence; or
      3.   Posting a notice at the owner or possessor's last known address.
   E.   Owner Not Found: If the sheriff cannot, with due diligence, locate the
owner of a dog that has been declared dangerous, or if the owner of such dog
shall fail or refuse to accept service of the required notice, the sheriff
shall cause the dog to be impounded for not less than ten (10) business days.
If, after ten (10) business days, the owner fails to claim the dog or accept
service of the required notice, the sheriff may cause the dog to be humanely
destroyed.
   F.   Contents Of Declaration: The declaration shall state at least:
      1.   A description of the dog.
      2.   The name and address of the owner or possessor of the dog, if known.
      3.   The whereabouts of the dog, if known, if such dog is not in the
custody of the owner.
      4.   A summary of the facts upon which the declaration that the dog is
dangerous is based.
      5.   The availability of a hearing before the board of county
commissioners in case the person objects to the declaration if a request is
made within five (5) calendar days; that the owner can be represented by an
attorney at all stages of the hearing; and that the owner can appeal an adverse
decision by the board of county commissioners to the district court in
accordance with this section.
      6.   The restrictions and conditions placed on the animal as a result of
the declaration that the dog is a dangerous dog and the date upon which the
owner shall be required to have complied with such restrictions.
      7.   With regard to a declaration of a dangerous dog that is determined
to be a threat to public safety, an order for euthanasia of the dog within five
(5) days unless an appeal is filed in the interim.
      8.   The penalties for violation of the restrictions, including the
possibility of destruction of the animal, and imprisonment or fining of the
owner.
   G.   Objection By Owner; Hearing Before The Board Of County Commissioners:
If the owner of the animal wishes to object to the declaration of a dangerous
dog by the sheriff:
      1.   The owner may, within five (5) days of receipt of the declaration,
request a hearing before the board of county commissioners by submitting a
written request to the sheriff.
      2.   Any facts which the petitioner wishes to be considered may be
submitted either in writing or orally at the hearing. The person seeking to
have the dog declared potentially dangerous or dangerous bears the burden of
persuasion by a preponderance of the evidence. The formal rules of evidence
shall not be applied but both parties shall have the right to present
testimony, ask questions, be represented at their own expense and appeal an
adverse ruling. After the hearing, the board of county commissioners shall make
a final determination whether the dog is or is not a "dangerous dog", as
defined in this chapter.
      3.   At the conclusion of a hearing conducted under this section, that
decision shall be final unless the dog owner applies to a court of competent
jurisdiction for any remedies that may be available.
   H.   Appeal: The owner of the animal has the right to appeal the board of
county commissioners' determination that a dog is dangerous.
      1.   The owner may, within five (5) days of receipt of the board of
county commissioners' written finding, request a hearing before the district
court by submitting a written request to the clerk of the court.
      2.   If the court finds that there is insufficient evidence to support
the declaration, it shall be rescinded and the restrictions imposed thereby
annulled, and the animal, if impounded, shall be released into the owner's
custody without payment of the impound fees.
      3.   If the court finds sufficient evidence to support the declaration,
it may impose court costs on the appellant, and may impose additional
restrictions or penalties on the animal or owner as provided herein.
      4.   In the event the court finds that the animal is not a dangerous dog,
no court costs shall be assessed against the county or the animal control
agency or officer.
      5.   Following service of a declaration of dangerous dog, the sheriff, if
circumstances require as a matter of public safety, shall impound the animal at
the owner's expense, pursuant to the provisions of this chapter, until a court
orders either its redemption or destruction.
   I.   Consequences Of A Dangerous Dog:
      1.   If the sheriff, his designee, or animal control officer determines
that a dog is a dangerous dog, or affirmed after appeal, the owner shall comply
with the requirements within this chapter.
      2.   If the sheriff, his designee, or animal control officer has probable
cause to believe a dog is a dangerous dog and may pose an immediate threat to
public safety, he may impound the dog pending final disposition of the case.
      3.   If a dangerous dog has been impounded and determined to pose a
threat to public safety, the sheriff may only return the dog to its owner if
the owner has:
         a.   Met the license requirements of section
5-5-2 of this chapter and, where applicable, agreed to comply with the
aforementioned requirements;
         b.   Met or agreed to comply with any additional security or care
requirements established by the sheriff, board of county commissioners, or
court.
      4.   The sheriff may humanely destroy a dog if:
         a.   The dog has been determined to be a threat to public safety if it
is returned to the owner;
         b.   The owner fails to comply with the registration requirements of
section
5-5-2 of this chapter; the requirements of section
5-5-3 of this chapter; or any special requirements imposed by the sheriff,
board of county commissioners, or court of law;
         c.   The owner fails to reimburse the county/animal control agency for
the costs and expenses of the dog's impoundment; or
         d.   The owner forfeits the dog for humane destruction. (Ord. 2017-1,
1-23-2017)
5-5-19: PENALTIES:
   A.   Except as provided herein, any person who violates any of the
provisions of this chapter, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and subject to
penalty as provided in this code for each offense.
   B.   A first offense conviction of allowing a dog to run at large in
violation of subsection
5-5-5A of this chapter or a first offense of harboring a barking dog in
violation of subsection
5-5-5C of this chapter, shall be deemed an infraction. A second or subsequent
offense of allowing a dog to run at large in violation of subsection
5-5-5A of this chapter or a second or subsequent offense of harboring a barking
dog in violation of subsection
5-5-5C of this chapter shall be a misdemeanor and subject to penalty as
provided in this code for each offense.
   C.   In addition to what is expressed herein, any dog which attacks a human
being, any domestic animal, or any livestock, may be ordered destroyed when, in
the court's judgment, such dog represents a continuing threat of harm to human
beings, domestic animals, or livestock. In addition, after a hearing, the judge
may order any dog destroyed which habitually creates a nuisance to any
neighborhood or person. The conviction of an owner for a second or subsequent
offense of allowing a dog to bark or create noise which is a nuisance to the
neighborhood or another person, shall be sufficient to establish that a dog
habitually creates a nuisance.
   D.   Any person found guilty of violating this chapter shall pay all
expenses, including shelter, food, any veterinary expenses necessitated by the
seizure of the dog for the protection of the public, and such other expenses as
may be required for the care or destruction of any such dog. (Ord. 2017-1, 1-
23-2017)
CHAPTER 6
EXOTIC ANIMALS
SECTION:
5-6-1: Definitions
5-6-2: Prohibited Acts
5-6-3: Penalties
5-6-1: DEFINITIONS:
WILD OR EXOTIC ANIMAL: Any animal which is wild, fierce, dangerous, noxious or
naturally inclined to do harm. "Wild animals", however domesticated, shall also
include, but not be limited to:
   A.   Dog family (Canidae): All except domesticated dogs, including wolf,
fox, coyote, dingo, wolf hybrids, etc.
   B.   Cat family (Felidae): All except commonly accepted domestic cats,
including lions, pumas, panthers, mountain lions, leopards, jaguars, ocelots,
margays, tigers, wild cats, etc.
   C.   Bears (Ursidae): All bears, including grizzly bears, brown bears, black
bears, etc.
   D.   Weasels (Mustelidae): All, including weasels, martens, mink, wolverine,
ferrets, badgers, otters, ermine, mongoose, etc.
   E.   Raccoons (Procyonidae): All raccoons and civets.
   F.   Porcupine (Erethizontidae): All porcupines.
   G.   Skunks.
   H.   Snakes: All venomous and constricting snakes.
   I.   Venomous lizards.
   J.   Crocodillians: All alligators, caimans, crocodiles, gavials, etc.
   K.   Venomous fish and piranha.
   L.   Venomous invertebrates. (Ord. 2005-4, 5-16-2005)
5-6-2: PROHIBITED ACTS:
It shall be unlawful for any person, corporate or entity to harbor, keep,
maintain or possess within the county of Payette any wild or exotic animal,
except those persons who are expressly licensed or permitted in writing by the
Idaho department of fish and game to keep and/or rehabilitate any such animal
so long as that person or persons are in compliance with the terms of such a
license and the animal kept or rehabilitated is domestic to the state of Idaho.
(Ord. 2005-4, 5-16-2005)
5-6-3: PENALTIES:
A person, firm, corporation or entity violating any of the provisions of this
chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof
shall be fined in an amount not exceeding three hundred dollars ($300.00) or be
imprisoned in the county jail for a period not exceeding six (6) months, or be
both so fined and imprisoned. (Ord. 2005-4, 5-16-2005)
CHAPTER 7
RECREATIONAL VEHICLES
SECTION:
5-7-1: Definitions
5-7-2: Residing In Recreational Vehicles Prohibited
5-7-3: Violation
5-7-1: DEFINITIONS:
"Recreational vehicle" means a motor home, travel trailer, truck camper or
camping trailer, with or without motive power, designed for human habitation
for recreational or emergency occupancy. School buses or van type vehicles
which are converted to recreational use are also defined as recreational
vehicles. (Ord. 2009-02, 4-13-2009)
5-7-2: RESIDING IN RECREATIONAL VEHICLES PROHIBITED:
For purposes of this chapter, a person shall be living, residing or staying in
a recreational vehicle if they use or occupy a recreational vehicle within
Payette County for thirty (30) or more days in any twelve (12) month period. No
person shall live, reside or stay in any recreational vehicle outside of a
licensed recreational vehicle park. (Ord. 2009-02, 4-13-2009)
5-7-3: VIOLATION:
Any violation of this chapter shall be a misdemeanor punishable by not more
than six (6) months in the Payette County jail or a fine of not more than one
thousand dollars ($1,000.00) or both. (Ord. 2009-02, 4-13-2009)
CHAPTER 8
TOW POLICY
SECTION:
5-8-1: Definitions
5-8-2: Driving Tow Truck To Scene Of Accident Prohibited Unless Called By
Dispatch
5-8-3: Soliciting Tow Business At Scene Of Law Enforcement Tow Prohibited
5-8-4: Response To Certain Private Calls For Towing Services Prohibited
5-8-5: Certain Remuneration Or Consideration Prohibited
5-8-6: Dispatch
5-8-7: Licensee Responsibilities
5-8-8: License Required; Expiration Date; Location
5-8-9: Eligibility And Requirements For Placement On Tow Rotation
5-8-10: License Application; Inspections; Issuance
5-8-11: Random Inspections; Violations; Suspensions; Revocations; Hearings
5-8-12: Tow Truck Specifications And Capabilities
5-8-13: Fees For Law Enforcement Towing
5-8-14: Requirements And Operating Procedures For Emergency Tow Companies
5-8-15: Use As Emergency Vehicle Prohibited
5-8-16: Penalties
5-8-17: Severability
5-8-18: When Effective
5-8-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following terms will have the following meanings:
ACCIDENT: Any occurrence in Payette County which results in a wrecked or
disabled vehicle, and which results in either the injury or death of any
person, or damage to property of any one person in excess of one thousand five
hundred dollars ($1,500.00), or both.
BUSINESS DAY: Monday through Friday excluding holidays declared by the Board of
Payette County Commissioners.
COMPANY OWNER: Any person who has an ownership interest in a business, meaning
a corporation; LLC; sole proprietor; partnership; or any other duly formed
organization under the laws of Idaho.
CONVICTION: Finding or plea of guilt, whether or not the sentence is imposed,
suspended, deferred, or withheld; and whether or not the case or charge is
dismissed under Idaho Code section 19-2604 or any comparable statute or
procedure.
DISABLED VEHICLE: A vehicle which has been abandoned or rendered unsafe to be
driven as the result of some occurrence other than an accident including, but
not limited to: a) mechanical failures or breakdowns; b) fire; c) vandalism; d)
a vehicle which is in a safe driving condition, but the owner is not present,
able or permitted to drive; or e) any other occurrence which reasonably
necessitates removal of the vehicle by a tow truck.
DISPATCH: The person or persons in the Payette County Sheriff's Office assigned
by the Sheriff to route law enforcement agency calls for tow truck service by
the use of tow truck rotation list.
EMERGENCY TOW COMPANY: A person to whom a law enforcement towing license has
been issued.
IMPOUND OFFICER: Any employee designated by the Payette County Sheriff to
handle law enforcement towing duties.
LAW ENFORCEMENT TOW: Provision of a tow truck to the owner of a wrecked or
disabled vehicle by dispatch when a law enforcement agency has become involved.
LICENSEE: A person licensed to engage in law enforcement towing as called to do
so from time to time by dispatch.
OWNER: A person who holds legal title to a vehicle, or who has legal right of
possession of a vehicle, or legal right of control of a vehicle.
PAYETTE COUNTY: That area which is within the jurisdiction of the Board of
Payette County Commissioners.
PERSON: An individual, assumed name entity, proprietorship, partnership, joint
venture, association, corporation, or other legal entity.
PERSONAL PROPERTY: Items that are not affixed to the vehicle such as, but not
limited to: papers, cellphones, portable radios, clothes, luggage, tools, or
other items.
TOW TRUCK: A vehicle designed to be used primarily for removing wrecked or
disabled vehicles from any street.
TOW TRUCK ROTATION LIST: A list of qualified licensed tow companies maintained
by dispatch and which is used to determine the priority of the tow truck to be
dispatched to the scene of a law enforcement tow. Only those businesses which
have a tow truck and tow truck driver located within Payette County shall be on
the rotation list. The business must also conform to subsection 5-8-8B of this
chapter.
WRECKED VEHICLE: A vehicle that has been damaged as the result of overturning
or colliding with another vehicle or object so as to reasonably necessitate the
vehicle be removed by a tow truck. (Ord. 2018-3, 3-26-2018; amd. Ord. 2023-07,
5-22-2023)
5-8-2: DRIVING TOW TRUCK TO SCENE OF ACCIDENT PROHIBITED UNLESS CALLED BY
DISPATCH:
No person may knowingly drive a tow truck, licensed or unlicensed, to the scene
of any accident or incident in Payette County for the purpose of removing a
vehicle from the area unless the tow truck has been called to the scene by
dispatch. (Ord. 2018-3, 3-26-2018; amd. Ord. 2023-07, 5-22-2023)
5-8-3: SOLICITING TOW BUSINESS AT SCENE OF LAW ENFORCEMENT TOW PROHIBITED:
No person may solicit in any manner, directly or indirectly, at the scene of a
law enforcement tow in Payette County, the business of towing, removing,
repairing, wrecking, storing, trading, or purchasing a vehicle. (Ord. 2018-3,
3-26-2018)
5-8-4: RESPONSE TO CERTAIN PRIVATE CALLS FOR TOWING SERVICES PROHIBITED:
A tow truck shall not knowingly respond to a private request for towing service
within the County when an accident is involved. A tow truck may respond to a
private request for towing service to a disabled vehicle not involved in an
accident, or to a private request for other towing services not requiring the
involvement of a law enforcement agency; provided, however, if, upon arrival on
the scene, a licensee discovers an accident is involved, the licensee shall
immediately notify dispatch. (Ord. 2018-3, 3-26-2018)
