5-8-5: CERTAIN REMUNERATION OR CONSIDERATION PROHIBITED:
Emergency tow companies are prohibited from soliciting or accepting any
remuneration or consideration of any type from any repair shop, garage or other
repair facility given for the purpose of influencing such emergency tow
company's decision as to where a disabled or wrecked vehicle should be taken
for repair. It shall be a rebuttable presumption that any such remuneration or
consideration was given for the purpose of influencing said decision. (Ord.
2018-3, 3-26-2018)
5-8-6: DISPATCH:
   A.   If a law enforcement officer determines a tow truck is needed at the
scene of a law enforcement tow for a wrecked or disabled vehicle, dispatch
shall call either the towing service, whether licensed or unlicensed, indicated
to the law enforcement officer by the express preference of the owner, or, if
the owner does not of his or her own initiative expressly request a particular
towing service, the next available emergency tow company on the tow truck
rotation list. Dispatch shall indicate to the emergency tow company the color,
year, make, body and general condition of the vehicle to be towed. Based on the
information provided, the tow company shall provide all necessary towing
equipment.
   B.   In order to be placed on the tow rotation the tow company must be able
to respond to a call from dispatch within thirty (30) minutes, or in a
reasonable time based upon road conditions and maintain a storage lot within
Payette County accessible within thirty (30) minutes from any portion of the
service area. (Ord. 2018-3, 3-26-2018; amd. Ord. 2023-07, 5-22-2023)
5-8-7: LICENSEE RESPONSIBILITIES:
   A.   Tow truck companies licensed to perform law enforcement towing are
responsible for wrecked and disabled vehicles and the contents therein, from
the time of on scene pick up until the vehicle is removed from licensee's
premises or is otherwise released from licensee's custody and control. Any
damage or loss to said vehicle or contents while in the custody and control of
licensee is the sole responsibility of licensee and Payette County assumes no
liability for any such loss or damage.
   B.   Turning Down A Call: If a tow truck turns down a call or is unable to
respond, it will be passed on its position on the rotation list. A tow service
may not refer its calls to another tow truck service.
   C.   Unavailability: If any tow company becomes unavailable for any reason,
the company may notify dispatch of the dates regarding their unavailability and
their rotation slots will be skipped during that time frame.
   D.   Indemnification: Each tow company on the rotation shall defend and
indemnify the county of Payette, and its officers, agents, employees, or other
individuals associated with the County of Payette for any claim against the
same arising out of a company's operation of a tow truck. (Ord. 2018-3, 3-26-
2018; amd. Ord. 2023-07, 5-22-2023)
5-8-8: LICENSE REQUIRED; EXPIRATION DATE; LOCATION:
   A.   No person may provide law enforcement towing inside the County without
first obtaining a law enforcement towing license. The license issued to an
emergency tow company authorizes the licensee and all its bona fide employees
to engage in dispatched law enforcement towing from the tow truck rotation
list. Only one license may be issued to each emergency tow company owner, and a
tow company owner can have no more than one tow company on the tow truck
rotation list at any point in time. Licensed tow companies may not subcontract
with other towing agencies, licensed or unlicensed, for the provision of law
enforcement towing services. Applications for law enforcement towing licenses
may be obtained at the Payette County Sheriff's Office beginning on May 1 of
each year, and all completed applications must be received by the Payette
County Sheriff no later than May 31 of each year. Incomplete applications will
not be accepted. Tow service inspections for the upcoming licensing year shall
be conducted by the Payette County Sheriff's Office during June of each year.
All such licenses shall expire on June 30 of the following calendar year. The
fee for said license shall be set by resolution of the Board of County
Commissioners.
   B.   Licensees shall maintain a permanent and established place of business
within Payette County, and shall promptly notify the Payette County Sheriff of
any change of address. (Ord. 2018-3, 3-26-2018; amd. Ord. 2023-07, 5-22-2023)
5-8-9: ELIGIBILITY AND REQUIREMENTS FOR PLACEMENT ON TOW ROTATION:
   A.   Tow truck companies must be established Idaho businesses, filed with
Idaho Secretary of State, or have a registered agent listed with the Idaho
Secretary of State.
   B.   The company name shall be prominently displayed on the driver's and
passenger's side doors and be permanently affixed to the vehicle.
   C.   Tow truck companies may not assign, contract, or utilize the services
of anyone to respond to a call or supervisor or safeguard items recovered under
this agreement who has been convicted of any offense:
      1.   That pertains to alteration or removal of a vehicle's identification
number, theft and/or injury to vehicles, unlawful possession of burglary tools,
petit theft, grand theft, robbery, arson, extortion, forgery, false
imprisonment, or burglary within the past ten (10) years.
      2.   Any offense, the elements of which include the infliction or threat
of bodily injury or death to a person or persons, including, but not limited
to, homicide, rape, assault, kidnapping, menacing or coercion within the past
ten (10) years.
      3.   Reckless driving or driving under the influence of any drug or
intoxicating liquor, regardless of whether the incident resulted in bodily
injury or death, hit and run, any drug use, possession or sale, and evading a
police officer within the preceding five (5) years.
      4.   Any crime, whether a felony or misdemeanor, that is a sex crime or
the elements of which would fall under Idaho's Sex Crime Statutes, including,
but not limited to, sexual assault, sexual harassment, sexual exploitation of a
minor, and child molestation. A sex crime includes, but is not limited to, any
offense for which an individual must register as a sex offender.
      5.   Any felony crime against property, including theft, or criminal
trespass, providing that such crime will be disqualifying only if: a) the
conviction occurred within the ten (10) years preceding the date of
determination, or b) the applicant or tow company agent/owner has any previous
conviction of such a crime.
   D.   No tow truck company can be placed on the rotation list if the Company
Owner of that towing company is also a Company Owner of another towing company
on the County's rotation list.
      1.   This includes a Company Owner that is a majority or minority owner.
      2.   This includes if the Company Owner is an executive of the towing
company previously placed on the rotation list.
      3.   This includes if the Company Owner's business is the parent company
of another towing company already on the rotation list.
      4.   This includes if the Company Owner's business is a subsidiary of
another towing company already on the rotation list.
   E.   Any person or tow service provider may seek a waiver of the
requirements outlined in subsection B C of this section by submitting a request
for waiver within fourteen (14) days of notification along with any evidence or
information the appealing party feels relevant to mitigate or refute the
disqualifier.
      1.   The inspection officer will review the information and make a
determination whether to grant or deny the requested waiver.
      2.   A denial may be appealed within fourteen (14) days from the denial
by the inspection officer to the Sheriff. A denial by the Sheriff will be
considered final. Failure to exhaust your administrative remedies will result
in a denial of your waiver.
   F.   Tow truck companies must submit the name, date of birth and social
security number of each driver for driver's status and criminal record checks.
(Ord. 2018-3, 3-26-2018; amd. Ord. 2023-07, 5-22-2023)
5-8-10: LICENSE APPLICATION; INSPECTIONS; ISSUANCE:
   A.   Contents Of Application: A person desiring to obtain a Payette County
law enforcement towing license shall lodge with the Payette County Sheriff a
written application upon a form provided for that purpose, which must be signed
by the applicant or his authorized agent. The following information shall be
required in the application:
      1.   Owner name, address to which all official correspondence may be
sent, telephone number and signature.
      2.   Company name, address and telephone number.
      3.   Number and types of tow trucks to be operated.
      4.   A statement as to whether or not the applicant wishes to participate
in the tow truck rotation list.
      5.   A copy of the applicant's public liability insurance policy.
      6.   A description of the applicant's impound yard and its location.
      7.   A copy of a valid driver's license of any person who may operate a
tow truck. This subsection places upon the licensee a continuing duty to
provide copies of valid driver's licenses.
   B.   Inspections: Upon the lodging of the application, the impound officer
shall direct the applicant to appear for an inspection of the tow truck(s) at a
time and place to be determined by the impound officer. The impound officer
shall conduct an inspection of the tow truck(s) and the business premises of
the applicant, as necessary, to determine if each tow truck and emergency tow
company complies with this chapter.
   C.   Action On Application: The impound officer may, at any time, in his or
her discretion, require additional information from an applicant to clarify
items on the application. Failure to cooperate with the impound officer's
request for additional information may result in the denial of a license. Upon
completion of the processing of the application, the impound officer shall
forward the application and the impound officer's recommendation to the Sheriff
for action thereon. The section shall not be deemed as placing any liability
upon Payette County or the Payette County Sheriff's Office. The County of
Payette shall have no liability under any theory of liability, for permitting
tow trucks to be operated on roads. Any person or company who operates a tow
truck is responsible for procuring liability insurance sufficient to cover any
foreseeable risk.
   D.   Issuance: The Sheriff shall, within thirty (30) days of receipt of an
application for a law enforcement towing license, either approve or deny said
application. The Sheriff shall issue a law enforcement towing license if the
Sheriff finds that the emergency tow company meets the requirements of this
chapter. The Sheriff shall refuse to issue or reissue a license if the Sheriff
finds that the emergency tow company does not meet the requirements of this
chapter. Upon issuance of a license, the tow company owner shall be provided
inspection stickers for each vehicle which passes the required inspection.
Annual inspection stickers must be displayed on the driver's side windshield of
each licensed tow truck. If at any time during the license year, an emergency
tow company violates the requirements of this chapter, the license may be
suspended or revoked in accordance with this chapter. (Ord. 2018-3, 3-26-2018)
5-8-11: RANDOM INSPECTIONS; VIOLATIONS; SUSPENSIONS; REVOCATIONS; HEARINGS:
   A.   Inspections: Any Payette County Sheriff's Deputy or the impound officer
is authorized to conduct random equipment and safety inspections of any tow
truck company licensed to conduct law enforcement tows.
   B.   Violations And Temporary Suspensions: The following violations shall
result in a written warning by the impound officer. Any repeat(s) of the same
violation shall result in an immediate temporary suspension from the tow truck
rotation list for a period not to exceed three (3) days. More than three (3)
repeats of the same violation shall result in the imposition of a license
revocation or suspension of more than three (3) days of licensee's law
enforcement tow license in accordance with subsection C of this section.
      1.   Failure to notify dispatch that tow company's on scene arrival time
will exceed thirty (30) minutes.
      2.   Failure to have the required equipment for each operating tow truck
and to have such equipment in good operating condition.
      3.   Use of magnetic striping/signage on tow trucks.
      4.   Listing more than one tow truck company on a tow truck.
      5.   Charging tow customers in excess of the tow rates established by the
Payette County Board of Commissioners for law enforcement tows.
      6.   Subcontracting law enforcement tows through other tow companies,
licensed or unlicensed.
      7.   Failing to comply with subsection
5-8-10  A.7. of this chapter.
      8.   Failure of any licensee or driver to obey a lawful order of a
Sheriff's Deputy or other police officer at the scene of an event wherein a tow
truck driver has been requested by Payette County Sheriff's Office or any other
police agency.
   C.   License Suspensions And Revocations: If the impound officer finds that
any of the following violations have been committed, the impound officer shall
issue an immediate twenty four (24) hour suspension of the licensee's law
enforcement tow license, and make a recommendation to the Sheriff or his
designee for revocation or suspension of said law enforcement tow license for
more than three (3) days:
      1.   Failure to respond to a dispatch request for a law enforcement tow
more than two (2) times in any calendar month.
      2.   Driving a tow truck to the scene of an accident without having been
requested to the scene by dispatch.
      3.   The solicitation of tow truck business by any licensee or employee
or agent of licensee at the scene of a law enforcement tow.
      4.   The failure to report an accident to dispatch for which a law
enforcement tow is required.
      5.   The solicitation or accepting of any remuneration or consideration
of any type by any licensee, employee or agent of a licensee, from any garage,
or repair shop or facility, for the purpose of influencing such licensee's
decision as to where a disabled or wrecked vehicle should be taken for repair.
      6.   Allowing the lapse or cancellation of the tow business insurance
required by this chapter.
      7.   Violation of any Federal, State or local law while conducting any
law enforcement tow.
      8.   Use of verbal abuse or physical force toward any citizen or officer
while conducting any law enforcement tow.
      9.   Failure to comply with section
5-8-9  of this chapter.
   D.   Notice Of Intent: Within five (5) days of the impound officer's
recommendation, if the Sheriff or his designee finds good cause that a
violation of subsection C of this section has occurred, the Sheriff shall issue
a notice of intent to suspend or revoke a law enforcement towing license. Said
notice shall provide a general description of the alleged violation(s) and the
date(s) of the alleged violations. Depending on the nature and extent of the
violation(s), the Sheriff, in his sole discretion, may permit licensee to
resume law enforcement towing pending any hearing on the matter.
   E.   Right To Hearing: A licensee shall have the right to a hearing prior to
the revocation or suspension of more than three (3) days of its law enforcement
towing license, in accordance with the procedures set forth in subsection F of
this section. If the licensee does not request a hearing, or does not follow
the procedures for requesting a hearing, said decision to suspend or revoke the
license shall be final, and shall be effective fifteen (15) days from the date
of the notice of intent. Any suspension shall be for a length of time as
determined by the Sheriff, and any revocation shall be for the remainder of the
current licensing year.
   F.   Hearing Procedures: A licensee may request a hearing before the Sheriff
or his designee prior to the suspension for more than three (3) days or
revocation of a law enforcement towing license, in accordance with the
procedures set forth in this section.
      1.   A licensee desiring such a hearing shall, within fifteen (15) days
of the date of the notice of intent to suspend or revoke a law enforcement
towing license, file a written request for hearing with the Payette County
Sheriff, together with a statement setting forth the factual basis and reasons
for licensee's appeal of the decision. A copy of the request for hearing shall
also be delivered to the impound officer.
      2.   The Sheriff or his designee shall conduct an informal public hearing
within thirty (30) days after a request for hearing has been filed. The
licensee and the Sheriff may be represented by an attorney. The licensee will
be afforded the opportunity to present evidence and testimony. The licensee
shall have no right to cross examine or confront witnesses, except in the
discretion of the Sheriff, nor shall the Idaho Rules of Evidence apply to such
hearings. In the Sheriff's discretion, the record of any such hearing may be
held open for a period of time, not to exceed seven (7) days, for the receipt
of additional evidence.
      3.   The Sheriff or his designee shall issue a written decision within
ten (10) days after the hearing. A copy of the decision shall be mailed or made
available to all interested parties. A record of said hearing and decision
shall remain in the custody of the Sheriff.
   G.   Removal from rotation: Once a law enforcement tow license has been
revoked, that company shall be removed from the rotation list. After a tow
company has been removed from the rotation list it is ineligible to participate
in the rotation list and must reapply during the next application period. (Ord.
2018-3, 3-26-2018; amd. Ord. 2023-07, 5-22-2023)
5-8-12: TOW TRUCK SPECIFICATIONS AND CAPABILITIES:
   A.   Compliance: Each emergency tow company shall comply with all safety
provisions, rules and regulations required to be observed by motor carriers,
and, in addition thereto, shall comply with the requirements of this chapter.
See the Payette County Sheriff's policy regarding tow truck specifications.
   B.   Equipment: Each tow truck shall be equipped with only those winches and
booms that have been produced and constructed by a manufacturer of such
equipment that regularly produces winches and tow equipment of guaranteed
quality and be used with the size tow truck for the class for which the
equipment is designed. All related equipment shall be commensurate with the
total rating of booms or other towing devices. (Ord. 2018-3, 3-26-2018)
5-8-13: FEES FOR LAW ENFORCEMENT TOWING:
Fees for services provided by licensed emergency tow companies pursuant to this
chapter shall be set by resolution of the Board of Payette County
Commissioners. (Ord. 2018-3, 3-26-2018)
5-8-14: REQUIREMENTS AND OPERATING PROCEDURES FOR EMERGENCY TOW COMPANIES:
Tow companies licensed to perform law enforcement tows must:
   A.   Maintain twenty-four (24) hour towing service, available seven (7) days
per week, with the dispatch of such service to be from base stations or an
answering service.
   B.   Not refuse to provide a law enforcement tow more than two (2) times in
any calendar month.
   C.   Arrive at the accident within a reasonable time after having been
notified to do so by dispatch. Such response time shall not exceed thirty (30)
minutes.
   D.   Maintain a tow truck and tow truck driver, at all times, within Payette
County.
   E.   Maintain its own separate locked, lighted and secured impound lot
bordered by a chain link, steel, or concrete fence not less than six feet (6')
in height; provided further that said lot shall be insured for fire, theft, and
vandalism of the vehicles stored therein and further, shall be open for
business not less than from nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. to five o'clock (5:00)
P.M. during business days. An agent of the emergency tow company must be on the
premises to conduct the business of the tow company during the above stated
days and hours.
   F.   The Payette County Sheriff's Office shall conduct an inventory of all
items contained in or on an impounded vehicle to be towed, on a form provided
by the Payette County Sheriff, the completion of said inventory form to be
witnessed and initialed by a tow company driver on the scene. All items
inventoried, which are not taken to Sheriff's property, shall remain in the
custody and control of the licensee until released to the owner. If any item(s)
is of an estimated value of one hundred dollars ($100.00) or more, and cannot
be secured in the vehicle, the property shall be taken to Sheriff's property
and a property invoice left in the vehicle or given to the vehicle owner, if
the owner is available, at the time the vehicle is impounded.
   G.   When authorized by the law enforcement agency, deliver, in every
instance, the wrecked or disabled vehicle to either a location of the owner's
choice or the tow company's impound lot. An itemized statement of charges shall
be provided to the vehicle owner upon request.
   H.   Report to the impound officer immediately all changes in tow trucks and
equipment used in the licensee's law enforcement towing service and make all
additional vehicles and equipment available for inspection by the impound
officer. A tow truck which has not been inspected by the impound officer is not
allowed to participate in the tow truck rotation list.
   I.   Before leaving the site of an accident, completely remove all resulting
wreckage or debris, including all broken glass.
   J.   Maintain two-way communications on a twenty-four (24) hour basis with
the company's tow trucks.
   K.   Meet the following insurance requirements:
      1.   At their sole expense, tow companies shall procure and maintain in
full force and effect, insurance written by an insurance company or companies
with Best's rating(s) of A VIII or better. All insurance companies must be
authorized to do business in the State of Idaho. By requiring insurance herein,
Payette County does not represent that coverage and/or limits are necessarily
adequate to protect the tow company and such coverage and/or limits shall not
be deemed as a limitation on the tow company's liability under the indemnities
granted to Payette County through this license.
      2.   Certificates of insurance evidencing the coverage required herein
shall be provided to Payette County prior to performing any towing services for
Payette County. All certificates must be signed by an authorized representative
of the tow company's insurance carrier and must state that the issuing company,
its agents, or representatives will provide Payette County thirty (30) days'
written notice prior to any policies being canceled. Renewal certificates must
be provided to Payette County within thirty (30) days after the effective date
of the renewal.
      3.   Certificates shall be mailed to:
         Payette County Sheriff's Office
         1130 3rd Avenue North, Room 101
         Payette, ID 83661
      4.   Certificates must evidence the following minimum coverage:
         a.   Workers' compensation insurance meeting the statutory
requirements of the State of Idaho.
         b.   Employers' liability insurance providing limits of liability in
the following amounts:
 
Bodily injury by accident $100,000.00 each accident
Bodily injury by disease  $500,000.00 policy limit
Bodily injury by disease  $100,000.00 each employee
 
      c.   Garage liability insurance providing limits of liability in the
following amounts:
 
Auto only, each accident            $1,000,000.00
Other than auto only, each accident $1,000,000.00
Other than auto only, aggregate     $3,000,000.00
 
   The garage liability policy shall be written on a standard ISO policy form,
or an equivalent form, providing coverage for liability arising from garage
operations including premises, operations, completed operations, personal
injury, advertising injury, and liability assumed under an insured contract
(including tort liability of another assumed in a contract). Auto coverage must
show symbols 27, 28, and 29 or a separate business automobile liability policy
also must be purchased.
   Alternatively, tow companies may produce a certificate of insurance
evidencing commercial general liability insurance providing limits of liability
in the following amounts:
 
General aggregate                         $2,000,000.00
Product/completed operations aggregate    $2,000,000.00
Personal and advertising injury liability $1,000,000.00
Per occurrence                            $1,000,000.00
Fire legal liability                      $50,000.00
 
   The commercial general liability ("CGL") insurance policy shall be written
on an "occurrence" form and shall cover liability arising from premises,
operations, independent contractors, products, completed operations, personal
injury, advertising injury, and liability assumed under an insured contract
(including tort liability of another assumed in a contract).
         d.   Business automobile liability insurance (required only if symbols
27, 28, and 29 are not shown for garage liability) providing bodily injury and
property damage liability coverage for not less than one million dollars
($1,000,000.00) each accident limit. Business automobile liability insurance
shall be written on a standard ISO policy form, or an equivalent form,
providing coverage for liability arising out of owned, hired, or non-owned
vehicles in connection with this agreement.
         e.   Garage keeper's liability insurance providing legal liability
coverage, including comprehensive and collision, of not less than one hundred
thousand dollars ($100,000.00) per location for customers' autos or auto
equipment while the licensee is attending, servicing, repairing, parking or
storing the customer's auto or auto equipment.
         f.   On hook/cargo insurance providing coverage for customers' autos
while being towed or transported by the tow company with limits in the
following amounts:
 
Light or medium duty truck $50,000.00
Heavy duty truck           $100,000.00
Extra heavy duty truck     $250,000.00
 
      5.   Payette County and its elected officials, agents, employees,
successors and assigns shall be named as additional insured under all policies
except workers' compensation and employers' liability.
   L.   Nothing in this chapter shall be construed as obligating the emergency
tow company to transport a disabled or wrecked vehicle when weather or road
conditions make it impractical, impossible or dangerous to the operator. (Ord.
2018-3, 3-26-2018; amd. Ord. 2023-07, 5-22-2023)
5-8-15: USE AS EMERGENCY VEHICLE PROHIBITED:
Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to permit operation of a tow truck
as an authorized emergency vehicle. (Ord. 2018-3, 3-26-2018)
5-8-16: PENALTIES:
   A.   Any person violating the provisions of sections
5-8-3  and/or
5-8-4  of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon
conviction thereof shall be punished as provided by Idaho Code, section 18-113
as it may from time to time be amended and/or re-titled.
   B.   Any violation of sections
5-8-1 ,
5-8-2 ,
5-8-6  -
5-8-9 ,
5-8-11 , and/or
5-8-14  shall be a misdemeanor punishable by not more than six (6) months in
the Payette County Jail or a fine of not more than one thousand dollars
($1,000.00) or both. (Ord. 2018-3, 3-26-2018; amd. Ord. 2023-07,5-22-2023)
5-8-17: SEVERABILITY:
The provisions of this chapter are hereby declared severable. In the event any
section is found to be invalid by a court of competent jurisdiction, such will
not affect the validity of the remaining sections contained herein. (Ord. 2018-
3, 3-26-2018)
5-8-18: WHEN EFFECTIVE:
This chapter shall become effective upon publication in one issue of a
newspaper of general circulation in Payette County. (Ord. 2018-3, 3-26-2018)
PA570   6t.txt
TITLE 6
COUNTY ROADS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
TRAFFIC RULES
SECTION:
6-1-1: Adoption Of Idaho Motor Vehicle Laws
6-1-2: Speed Limit
6-1-1: ADOPTION OF IDAHO MOTOR VEHICLE LAWS:
   A.   Intent: It is hereby declared to be the intent of the governing body of
the county to aid and assist by whatever means possible, for the utmost
consistency in traffic regulation among and between agencies of the state
having such jurisdiction. Toward that end, adoption of the Idaho motor vehicle
laws by the counties is a necessary means of assuring maximum uniformity within
the state.
   B.   Adoption: There is hereby adopted for the purpose of establishing rules
and regulations for the use of all streets and public thoroughfares of the
county that certain code, identified as the Idaho motor vehicle laws, more
particularly title 49, Idaho Code, published by the department of law
enforcement, and as the same may hereafter be revised by the Idaho legislature,
or amended by the governing body, and the same is hereby adopted and
incorporated as though fully set forth at length herein.
   C.   Copies On File: Three (3) copies of the Idaho motor vehicle laws,
together with any revisions or amendments, duly certified by the county clerk,
shall be kept on file in her office for use and examination of and by the
public. (Ord. 10, 3-22-1971, eff. 3-29-1971; amd. 1996 Code)
6-1-2: SPEED LIMIT:
The speed of any motor vehicle in excess of fifty five (55) miles per hour on
highways outside urban districts, except state highways, shall be prima facie
evidence that the speed is not reasonable or prudent and that it is unlawful.
(Ord. 2005-5, 12-12-2005)
CHAPTER 2
ROADWAY CONSTRUCTION STANDARDS
SECTION:
6-2-1: Intent
6-2-2: Adoption Of Standards
6-2-3: Copies On File
6-2-1: INTENT:
It is hereby declared to be the intent of the board of county commissioners and
of the governing body of highway district no. 1, to establish uniform standards
for the construction of roadways within the county. Toward that end, adoption
of a uniform set of standards by the board of county commissioners and highway
district no. 1 is deemed necessary. (Ord. 37, 5-2-1983, eff. 5-11-1983)
6-2-2: ADOPTION OF STANDARDS:
There is hereby adopted for the purpose of establishing uniform construction
standards and regulations within the county and highway district no. 1 within
Payette County, those certain standards identified as the "roadway standards
and development procedures for Payette County road and bridge and highway
district no. 1". Such standards are hereby adopted and incorporated as a part
hereof as fully as though set forth at length. (Ord. 37, 5-2-1983, eff. 5-11-
1983; amd. Ord. 2000-4, 2-7-2000; Ord. 2008-02, 2-11-2008)
6-2-3: COPIES ON FILE:
Three (3) copies of the highway standards and development procedures for
Payette County road department and highway district no. 1, duly certified by
the county clerk, shall be kept on file in the county clerk's office for use
and examination of and by the public. (Ord. 37, 5-2-1983, eff. 5-11-1983; amd.
Ord. 2000-4, 2-7-2000)
CHAPTER 3
HIGHWAY RIGHTS OF WAY; ENCROACHMENTS
SECTION:
6-3-1: Policy
6-3-2: Definition
6-3-3: Minimum Width
6-3-4: Right-Of-Way Use
6-3-5: Restricted Activities
6-3-6: Adequacy Of Roads Serving Proposed Developments
6-3-7: Nuisance Conditions Prohibited
6-3-8: Damage To Highway Prohibited
6-3-9: Penalty
6-3-1: POLICY:
The policy of the governing body of the County and Payette County Highway
District #1 is set forth as follows:
   A.   To establish a highway right-of-way policy which will further public
safety, provide for orderly growth and protect the public investment in the
public roads and bridges of the County.
   B.   To provide freely passable public roads for all emergency and service
vehicles.
   C.   To prohibit the creation of unsafe conditions on or beside the public
roads of the County by new construction on or along said roads and to mitigate
any unsafe conditions presently existing on or along said roads. (Ord. 58, 5-
23-1988, eff. 5-26-1988)
6-3-2: DEFINITION:
A "public road" is one that has been laid out and recorded as road or highway
by order of a board of commissioners, or a road used as a highway for a
continuous period of five (5) years provided it shall have been worked and kept
up at the expense of the public, or located and recorded by order of a board of
commissioners. (Ord. 58, 5-23-1988, eff. 5-26-1988)
6-3-3: MINIMUM WIDTH:
   A.   Unrecorded Rights Of Way: All unrecorded road rights of way shall have
a minimum width of fifty feet (50').
   B.   Recorded Rights Of Way: Recorded rights of way may vary in width. The
road or highway shall consist of the entire width within the right of way, not
merely the traveled portion thereof.
   C.   Standards For Acceptance: No future road shall be accepted by the
County or by Payette County Highway District #1 (hereinafter referred to as
"District") as a public road unless it meets the standards established by
Chapter 2 of this Title. (Ord. 58, 5-23-1988, eff. 5-26-1988)
6-3-4: RIGHT-OF-WAY USE:
Any use of a road right of way other than a travelway use constitutes an
obstruction or encroachment and to the extent that such obstructions or
encroachments are incompatible with the safe usage of a public road right of
way the same shall be prohibited by the County and the District.
   A.   Obstructions: Obstructions or partial obstructions within a right of
way which are prohibited shall include, but are not necessarily limited to, the
following:
      1.   Livestock loading or feeding.
      2.   Crop harvesting, planting or other farm activities.
      3.   Parking for social functions, auctions, recreational activities or
gatherings or any other reason for longer than eight (8) hours during any
twenty four (24) hour time period.
   B.   Encroachments: Encroachments within a right of way which are prohibited
shall include, but are not necessarily limited to, the following:
      1.   Fences, hedges, shrubbery, and trees.
      2.   Crop plantings.
      3.   Irrigation head or waste articles, sprinklers, control structures or
other irrigation appurtenances.
      4.   Decorative structures and commercial or other private signs as
prohibited within the right of way by title 7, chapter 3 of this code.
      5.   Disposal of irrigation water in borrow pits. (Ord. 58, 5-23-1988,
eff. 5-26-1988; amd. 1996 Code)
      6.   Endangerment through landslide or potential landslide creation by
creating excessively steep cut or fill banks on adjacent property. "Roadway
standards and development procedures for Payette County road and bridge and
highway district no. 1" adopted in chapter 2 of this title, allows for adequate
size right of way for cut and fill sections plus ten feet (10') while
prohibiting damages to the roadway and providing for repair. (Ord. 58, 5-23-
1988, eff. 5-26-1988; amd. 1996 Code; Ord. 2000-4, 2-7-2000; Ord. 2008-02, 2-
11-2008)
      7.   Mailbox supports more rigid than freestanding wood posts of ordinary
size, six inches by six inches (6" x 6").
      8.   Irrigation pipelines parallel with roads within the right of way.
      9.   Piles of wood, fruit boxes or any other objects or materials that
create a safety hazard.
   C.   Removal:
      1.   Request For Removal: In the event such obstructions prevent the safe
or timely passageway of the public, the road superintendent having jurisdiction
shall request the abutting property owner to remove or correct the obstruction
within thirty (30) days.
      2.   Failure To Comply: If the abutting property owner does not comply,
the county or district may petition the court for an order directing the
property owner to remove or correct the obstruction.
      3.   Removal By County Or District; Costs: After thirty (30) days the
county or district may make the necessary removal, repairs and/or corrections
and assess the cost incurred to the responsible party.
      4.   Court Costs: Any court costs incurred shall be paid by the
responsible party.
      5.   Repairs Or Corrections: Any repairs or corrections shall be in
accordance with the construction standards adopted in section 6-2-2 of this
title. (Ord. 58, 5-23-1988, eff. 5-26-1988; amd. 1996 Code)
6-3-5: RESTRICTED ACTIVITIES:
   A.   Power To Restrict: To further the policies set forth above, the county
and the district may restrict installation and construction activities within
public rights of way.
   B.   Permit Required: Any such activity shall not be commenced without
application for and receipt of a permit from the road superintendent having
jurisdiction.
   C.   Standards: Any such activity shall be completed in accordance with the
standards adopted in chapter 2 of this title, or in the absence of any existing
county or district standard, in accordance with sound engineering principles.
   D.   Restricted Activities: Restricted activities shall include, but shall
not necessarily be limited to, installation or construction of the following:
      1.   Utility lines.
      2.   Potable water mains and services.
      3.   Sanitary sewer mains and services.
      4.   Storm sewer and culverts.
      5.   Electrical power lines, whether overhead or underground.
      6.   Telephone lines, whether overhead or underground.
      7.   Natural gas mains, laterals, services and other appurtenances.
      8.   Cable television lines.
      9.   Irrigation pipelines and siphons crossing roads.
      10.   Storm water or other drain pipes.
      11.   Driveway approaches (no more than 100 feet from an intersection)
must be constructed and drained to meet county standards. (Ord. 58, 5-23-1988,
eff. 5-26-1988)
6-3-6: ADEQUACY OF ROADS SERVING PROPOSED DEVELOPMENTS:
The safety of present neighboring residents and adequacy of roads leading to
the primary highway system are necessary and material considerations in
assessing the acceptability of any proposed residential, commercial, or
industrial development under zoning review and other approval procedures
provided by statutes and Chapter 2 of this Title and Title 9 of this Code,
thereby making it the duty of the person proposing development to show that no
unsafe condition or overload of existing facilities will be created by his/her
proposed development. In cases where either the County or the District finds
that unsafe or overload conditions will be created by a proposed development,
it is the policy of the County and the District to prevent the occurrence of
such conditions, either by denying license for the development or by
negotiating to obtain upgrading of the County road system in the vicinity of
the development. (Ord. 58, 5-23-1988, eff. 5-26-1988)
6-3-7: NUISANCE CONDITIONS PROHIBITED:
Endangering nuisances and damaging or unsafe conditions which originate from
adjacent properties shall be prohibited. These nuisances and conditions shall
include, but are not necessarily limited to, the following:
   A.   Drainage or irrigation water overflowing onto the roadway. Excess
sediment, and animal wastes should not be allowed to build up and block
drainage pipes. If the blockage constitutes a hazard, the removal of the hazard
will be at the expense of whosoever created the problem. When drain ditches and
irrigation ditches run parallel with rights of way, dirt and cleaning materials
from ditch maintenance shall not be put on the road right of way. Blockage of
drainage pipes in the right of way by irrigation pipelines, or other pipes such
as stock watering pipes, hoses, electrical wires or other foreign objects is
prohibited.
   B.   Foreign objects shall not be attached to bridges.
   C.   Visibility impairment from dust, water from sprinkler, steam and smoke.
   D.   Nuisances such as mud causing slippery conditions, dumping of garbage.
   E.   Defacing of road signs or placement of other signs (yard sales or
auctions) upon road signs. (Ord. 58, 5-23-1988, eff. 5-26-1988)
6-3-8: DAMAGE TO HIGHWAY PROHIBITED:
Damaging of the highway is prohibited. This includes farm machinery not mounted
on rubber tires, such as harrows and discs or any equipment with cleated
tracks, and backhoe outriggers that are not padded. Any other object that will
damage roadways is not to be dragged or driven or used on any paved surface.
(Ord. 58, 5-23-1988, eff. 5-26-1988)
6-3-9: PENALTY:
Any person convicted of a violation of any provision of this Chapter shall be
subject to penalty as provided in Section 1-4-1 of this Code. Either or both
such fine and imprisonment may be imposed; and in addition thereto, any person
so convicted shall pay such costs as the Court may assess, together with
restitution for any damages caused by said violation. (Ord. 58, 5-23-1988, eff.
5-26-1988; 1996 Code)
CHAPTER 4
COUNTY ROAD USE
SECTION:
6-4-1: River Road Use Restrictions
6-4-2: Use By Aircraft Prohibited
6-4-3: Parking Restrictions; Penalty
6-4-1: RIVER ROAD USE RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Purpose: The purpose of this section is to restrict the use of River
Road by semitractor trailers for the following reasons:
      1.   River Road is a narrow winding road used primarily by persons who
live on River Road, farmers and sportsmen.
      2.   River Road was not built to withstand heavy use or traffic of loaded
and unloaded semitractor trailers.
      3.   Semitractor trailers cause severe damage to the shoulders of River
Road.
      4.   Semitractor trailers are long vehicles which make the use of River
Road dangerous to other travelers.
      5.   Alternative routes over roads better suited to handle semitractor
trailers exist.
      6.   Those alternative routes will not impede or delay the travel of
semitractor trailer traffic in the county.
      7.   This section will not restrict or limit the use of semitractor
trailers for those persons living on, farming or conducting business on River
Road.
   B.   Definitions: As used in this section, the following words and terms
shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection:
   DESTINATION: The point of disembarkation for a semitractor trailer.
   RIVER ROAD: A Payette County road located north of the city of Payette,
running along the Snake River.
   SEMITRACTOR TRAILER: Any motorized vehicle classified in the bridge
maintenance and inspection manual of the Idaho department of transportation as
a type 3-S-2, which shall specifically also include all three (3) axle tractors
and two (2) axle trailers.
   STARTING POINT: The point where a semitractor trailer begins its travel on
any city, county or state road.
   C.   Closed To Through Traffic: Any semitractor trailer whose starting point
does not begin or whose destination does not end on River Road shall be
prohibited from operating and/or driving on River Road.
   D.   Posting: Payette Country road and bridge department is hereby
authorized to take all measures necessary to place signs along River Road
posting the restrictions created by this section.
   E.   Penalty: The penalty for a violation of this section shall be as
provided in section 1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 77, 8-17-1992, eff. 8-20-1992;
amd. 1996 Code)
6-4-2: USE BY AIRCRAFT PROHIBITED:
   A.   Definition: "Aircraft" is defined as any contrivance now known, or
hereafter invented, used or designed for navigation of or flight in the air.
   B.   Use For Landing; Exception: It is unlawful for the owner, lessee, or
operator of any aircraft to land an aircraft on a public road or highway within
the county, with the exception of a forced landing.
   C.   Use As Runway: It is unlawful for the owner, lessee, or operator of any
aircraft to use any public road or highway within the county as a runway.
   D.   Damages: Any damages caused by the use of public roads and/or highways,
as prohibited herein, whether to persons or property, shall be borne by the
owner, lessee and/or operator in accordance with the rules of law applicable to
torts on land in this state.
   E.   Penalty: Any violation of this section shall be a misdemeanor
punishable in accordance with the general misdemeanor statutes of the state. In
addition, any person who suffers damage by virtue of a violation of this
section may sue for damages and if successful shall be awarded all attorney
fees and costs. (Ord. 66, 7-9-1990)
6-4-3: PARKING RESTRICTIONS; PENALTY:
It is unlawful for any person to park a truck tractor, as defined by Idaho Code
section 49-121(10)(e), a pole trailer, as defined by Idaho Code section 49-121
(6)(e), or semitrailer, as defined by Idaho Code section 49-121(6)(f), on the
street or street right of way in the area known as "Vistair Subdivision".
Temporary parking shall be allowed for the purpose of loading or unloading, but
such temporary parking shall not exceed one hour. A violation of this section
shall constitute an infraction and shall be processed by the sheriff or the
sheriff's deputies in accordance with the Idaho infraction rules and the
current Idaho infraction penalty schedule, and as amended. Such infractions are
punishable by fixed penalty, which includes court costs for each offense in
accordance with the Idaho infraction rules and the current Idaho infraction
penalty schedule, and as amended. (Ord. 2001-4, 7-2-2001)

IMPROVEMENT DISTRICTS
ARTICLE A. LOCAL IMPROVEMENT DISTRICT 01-01

The purpose of this article is to create local improvement district 01-01
(hereinafter sometimes referred to as "LID 01-01") in an area known as Sabin
Road, Sandhollow, Payette County, Idaho. The intention of the local improvement
district is to build an asphalt road over what is currently referred to as
Sabin Road, for the safety and convenience of the residents who live along said
Sabin Road. (Ord. 2001-3, 3-19-2001)

6-5A-3: LOCATION OF ROAD IMPROVEMENT:
The road shall be built at the following location:
STARTING AT THE SOUTHWEST CORNER OF SECTION 36, T6N, R4W, BOISE MERIDIAN,
TRAVELING NORTH 4290 FEET ALONG THE BOUNDARY OF SECTION 35 AND 36, THEN SOUTH
330 FEET, THEN TRAVELING EAST N. 89°57'32" E. 1320 FEET IN SECTION 36 TO THE
END OF THE IMPROVEMENT.
(Ord. 2001-3, 3-19-2001)
6-5A-4: GENERAL DESCRIPTION OF IMPROVEMENTS:
The length of the road improvement shall be approximately five thousand two
hundred eighty feet (5,280'). The finished surface shall be twenty four feet
(24') wide. Ten inches (10") of pit run shall be used as a base, three inches
(3") of 3/4 minus for the leveling surface, and three inches (3") of asphalt
pavement. A barrow ditch shall be constructed on both sides of the road. (Ord.
2001-3, 3-19-2001)
6-5A-5: COST OF CONSTRUCTION AND ASSESSMENTS:
   A.   Formula: The probable cost for construction is two hundred ninety seven
thousand five hundred dollars ($297,500.00). The total cost and expenses of the
improvements are to be made and upon lots and lands benefited by such
improvements so that each of the parcels of land in the district be assessed
according to a combination of the square foot and front foot methods in
proportion to the benefits derived by each parcel. Specifically, the formula
used shall be as follows:
      ((.20 x total cost) x available residences/total residences) + ((.20
total cost) x square footage/total square footage) + ((.10 x total cost) x
zone/(total number of properties in zone) + ((.50 x total cost)/total users) =
assessment;
      with the following definitions:
         Available Residence: Some properties located in LID are eligible for
building permits for an additional residence. If the property is not eligible,
the available split quotient equals zero.
         Square Footage: The individual square footage of each property in LID.
         Total Cost: The total cost of the improvement.
         Total Residence: The total number of properties that have an available
residence.
         Total Square Footage: The total square footage of all properties in
LID.
         Zone: The entire road has been separated into two (2) zones. Those
properties receiving direct access from the road are in zone 1 and those not
receiving direct access from the road are in zone 2. (Ord. 2001-3, 3-19-2001)
   B.   Confirmation Of Assessment Roll: The assessment roll, attached to
ordinance 2002-6 as exhibit A, is confirmed. Each lot or parcel included within
local improvement district 01-01 is benefited by the improvements and the
benefit is equal to the amount assessed. Any person who has not paid the
assessment in full within thirty (30) days from August 26, 2002, shall be
conclusively presumed to have chosen to pay in installments. The period of
repayment shall be for ten (10) years and the interest rate shall be calculated
at five percent (5%) per annum. The first payment shall be due and payable on
October 1, 2003. Each payment thereafter shall be due and payable October 1
every year thereafter. Monthly payments may be made to the treasurer. Any
payment not made within twenty (20) days of the due date shall be deemed
delinquent and the treasurer shall add a penalty of two percent (2%) thereto.
(Ord. 2002-6, 8-28-2002)
6-5A-6: LATECOMER'S FEE:
   A.   Fee: Any person or entity who builds upon or develops real property, in
any manner, within local improvement district 01-01 (hereinafter "LID"), who
receives a benefit from the Tower Road and East Tower Road, formerly known as
Sabin Road, improvement and did not participate in financing the original
construction, shall be required to pay two thousand dollars ($2,000.00) per
building permit or improvement, hereinafter known as a "latecomer's fee". The
latecomer's fee shall be made in addition to any payment(s) made for a building
permit(s), transfer(s) of development right, and/or any other fee(s) required
by planning and zoning or the county commissioners. Payment of the latecomer's
fee shall be made to the Payette County treasurer prior to the issuance of a
building permit and/or any new construction and/or development.
      1.   Property owners who have paid their share(s) in full and have not
split the property more than one time shall receive a pro rata portion of any
latecomer's fee. In the event a parcel is split or divided one time, the
latecomer's fee shall be distributed to the recorded owner or owners.
      2.   Property owners who have not paid their portion of the cost in full
at the time a latecomer's fee is charged shall receive a pro rata deduction
from their outstanding principal, provided however, that if a parcel is in
arrears or default, the latecomer's fee for that parcel shall be allocated the
past due principal and interest and late fees.
   B.   Exemptions: The following shall not be considered latecomers for the
purpose of this section:
      1.   A building or improvement erected upon a parcel which had an
existing eligibility for a building permit(s) as of August 1, 2002.
      2.   A building or improvement erected upon a parcel which was not split
or divided after August 1, 2002, and which did not have an existing eligibility
to a building permit as of August 1, 2002, but obtained a permit through a
transfer of development rights.
      3.   A building or improvement erected upon a parcel which had an
existing eligibility for two (2) building permits as of August 1, 2002, and was
split or divided not more than one time after August 1, 2002.
      4.   Any person who was an original owner of property as of August 1,
2002.
All other improvements shall be deemed as latecomers and shall be assessed the
latecomer's fee.
   C.   Definitions:
   EXISTING ELIGIBILITY: The building right(s) which was included in and which
received an additional assessment in LID 01-01.
   PRO RATA: A percentage of the total cost the original parcel contributed to
LID 01-01.
   D.   Parcel Split: For a second or subsequent split, short plat or
subdivision, the entire assessment shall be paid in full prior to final
approval. The latecomer's fee must be paid in full prior to the development of
each parcel.
   E.   Distribution Of Fee: Distribution of latecomer's fee shall be made
annually, as determined by the Payette County treasurer.
   F.   Severability: If any portion of this section is found to be
unenforceable or unconstitutional for any reason, the remaining portion of this
section shall remain in full force and effect.
   G.   Duration: This section shall be in effect until July 29, 2012. (Ord.
2002-5, 8-5-2002)
CHAPTER 6
PAYETTE COUNTY GREENWAY
SECTION:
6-6-1: Defined
6-6-2: Prohibited Acts Relating To Greenway Property
6-6-3: Recreational Activities
6-6-4: Behavior
6-6-5: Merchandising, Advertising And Signs
6-6-6: Closed Areas
6-6-7: Enforcement
6-6-8: Penalties
6-6-1: DEFINED:
The "Payette County greenway" is property which is owned, operated or
maintained by the county of Payette and is located within the county of
Payette, Idaho, for public use as a footpath which runs along the Snake River
and Payette River in Payette County, Idaho. This definition includes any
federal or state owned properties which are included in the greenway. (Ord.
2003-7, 7-14-2003)
6-6-2: PROHIBITED ACTS RELATING TO GREENWAY PROPERTY:
No person shall:
   A.   Buildings Or Other Property:
      1.   Disfiguration And Removal: Wilfully mark, deface, disfigure, injure,
tamper with, or displace or remove, any building, bridges, tables, benches,
railings, paving or paving material, water lines or other public utilities or
parts or appurtenances whatsoever, either real or personal, or have in his
possession any of the foregoing things or objects, or any part thereof.
   B.   Trees, Shrubbery And Lawns:
      1.   Injury And Removal: Damage, cut, carve, transplant or remove any
tree or plant or injure the bark, or pick the flowers or seeds, of any tree or
plant. Nor shall any person attach any rope, wire or other contrivance to any
tree or plant. A person shall not dig in or otherwise disturb grass areas, or
in any other way injure or impair the natural beauty or usefulness of any area.
   C.   Wild Animals, Birds, Livestock, Etc.:
      1.   Hunting: Hunt, molest, harm, frighten, kill, trap, chase, tease,
annoy, shoot or throw missiles at any animal, reptile or bird nor shall he
remove or have in his possession the young of any wild animal, or the eggs or
nest, or young of any reptile or bird.
      2.   Feeding: Give or offer, or attempt to give to any animal or bird any
tobacco, alcohol or other known noxious substances.
      3.   Livestock: No person shall allow any livestock to become a stray or
estray. "Stray or estray" means any livestock whose owner is unknown or cannot
be located, or any livestock whose owner is known but who permits livestock to
roam at large upon the greenway. (Ord. 2003-7, 7-14-2003)
6-6-3: RECREATIONAL ACTIVITIES:
No person in the greenway shall:
   A.   Hunting And Firearms: Use firearms of any descriptions, or air rifles,
spring guns, bow and arrows, slings or any other forms of weapons potentially
inimical to wildlife and dangerous to human safety, or any instrument that can
be loaded with and fire blank cartridges, or any kind of trapping device; or
discharge, or have in his possession, any fireworks defined by section
5-3-1 of this code; or shoot into greenway areas from beyond park boundaries;
provided that it shall be lawful for police officers while on duty to use and
carry firearms.
   B.   Camping: Set up tents, shacks, or any other temporary shelter for the
purpose of camping, nor shall any person bring onto the greenway any movable
structure or special vehicle to be used, or that could be used, for such
purpose such as house trailer, camp trailer, camp wagon, or the like.
   C.   Games: Take part in or abet the playing of any games involving thrown
or otherwise propelled dangerous objects such as stones, arrows or javelins.
   D.   Horseback Riding: Ride a horse.
   E.   Motorized Vehicles: Operate a motorized vehicle, including, but not
limited to, cars, trucks, vans, snowmobiles, motorcycles and golf carts.
Exception is hereby made for emergency or other duly authorized vehicles. (Ord.
2003-7, 7-14-2003)
6-6-4: BEHAVIOR:
No person in the greenway shall:
   A.   Possess or consume any alcoholic beverage.
   B.   Permit or allow a dog or other domestic animal to enter or remain in
the greenway except on a leash and/or carried while leashed by such person
owning or having the care, custody and control of such dog or domestic animal.
The owner or person having possession of any dog or other domestic animal on
the greenway shall remove any feces left by such animal.
   C.   Endanger the safety or health of any person by any conduct or act,
including, but not necessarily limited to, urinating or defecating in, on or
upon the greenway, except when using an enclosed bathroom facility authorized
by the county.
   D.   Prevent any person from using the greenway, or any of its facilities,
or interfere with such use in compliance with this chapter and the rules and
regulations applicable to such use.
   E.   Solicit or accost other persons for the purpose of begging or
soliciting alms. (Ord. 2003-7, 7-14-2003)
   F.   Operate or aid in the operation of private radios, stereophonic or
sound amplification devices at a greater operating level than seventy five (75)
decibels measured at a distance of twenty feet (20') from such radios or
devices. (Ord. 2003-10, 10-14-2003)
   G.   Enter, or stay upon, the greenway during times when the greenway is
closed. The greenway shall be closed one hour after sunset and shall not be
open to the public until sunrise.
   H.   Litter, as defined by sections
4-6-1 through and including
4-6-3 of this code.
   I.   Engage in any unlawful conduct or criminal activity or in any way
commit a violation or breach of the peace, as defined by Idaho Code and/or this
code. (Ord. 2003-7, 7-14-2003)
6-6-5: MERCHANDISING, ADVERTISING AND SIGNS:
No person shall:
   A.   Vending And Peddling: Expose or offer for sale any article or thing,
nor shall he station or place any stand, cart or vehicle for the
transportation, sale or display of any such article or thing. Exception is here
made as to any regularly licensed concessionaire acting by and under the
authority of the Payette County board of commissioners.
   B.   Advertising: Distribute, leave or throw any advertising material, such
as dodgers, handbills, circular or like matter, or give away or otherwise
distribute for advertising purposes any goods or wares.
   C.   Signs: Paste, glue, tack or otherwise post any signs, plaques,
advertisement or inscription whatever, except plaques, tablets or signs, of a
size, design and location approved by the Payette County board of
commissioners, recognizing or acknowledging donations or contributions to the
greenway. (Ord. 2003-7, 7-14-2003)
6-6-6: CLOSED AREAS:
Any section or part of the greenway may be declared closed to the public by the
Payette County board of commissioners at any time and for any interval of time,
either temporarily or at regularly and stated intervals (daily or otherwise)
and either entirely or merely to certain uses. (Ord. 2003-7, 7-14-2003)
6-6-7: ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Officials: Payette County police officers and duly authorized police
officers from another jurisdiction, shall enforce the provisions of this
chapter.
   B.   Ejectment: A police officer shall have the authority to eject from the
greenway any person acting in violation of this chapter. Any person ejected
from the greenway shall leave promptly and peaceably and shall not return to
the greenway for any reason on the same calendar day of his ejectment.
   C.   Seizure Of Property: A police officer shall have the authority to seize
and confiscate any property, thing or device in the greenway, or used in
violation of this chapter. (Ord. 2003-7, 7-14-2003)
6-6-8: PENALTIES:
A person, firm or corporation violating any of the provisions of this chapter
shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be
fined in an amount not exceeding three hundred dollars ($300.00) or be
imprisoned in the city jail for a period not exceeding six (6) months, or be
both so fined and imprisoned. Nothing in this chapter shall be construed as to
limit county employees or other authorized persons from performing their
official or county authorized duties. (Ord. 2003-7, 7-14-2003)
TITLE 7
BUILDING REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
BUILDING CODES
SECTION:
7-1-1: Adoption Of Codes; Penalty
7-1-2: Substandard Roads, Building Permits Restricted
7-1-3: Zoning Certificate Required For Utilities
7-1-4: Rebar Requirements
7-1-1: ADOPTION OF CODES; PENALTY:
   A.   Codes Adopted:
      1.   Building Code: The 2018 version of the International Building Code,
prepared by the International Code Council, Inc., as adopted by the State of
Idaho or the Idaho Building Code Board, together with any amendments or
revisions to the International Building Code made by the Idaho Building Code
Board through the negotiated rulemaking process;
      2.   Residential Code: The 2018 version of the International Residential
Code, prepared by the International Code Council, Inc., as adopted by the State
of Idaho or the Idaho Building Code Board, together with any amendments or
revisions to the International Residential Code made by the Idaho Building Code
Board through the negotiated rulemaking process; excepting therefrom part VII
and VIII as those sections pertain to electrical and plumbing matters.
      3.   Energy Conservation Code: The 2018 version of the International
Energy Conservation Code, together with any amendments or revisions to the
International Energy Conservation Code made by the Idaho Building Code Board
through the negotiated rulemaking process;
      4.   Abatement Of Dangerous Buildings: The current version of the
International Building Code for the Abatement of Dangerous Buildings, published
by the International Conference of Building Officials;
      5.   Fuel And Gas Code: The 2018 version of the International Fuel and
Gas Code, together with appendices thereto;
      6.   Manufactured Home Installation Standard: The current version of the
State of Idaho Division of Building Safety Manufactured Home Installation
Standard, together with appendices thereto;
      7.   Recreational Vehicle Parks And Campgrounds: The current version of
the American National Standard for Recreational Vehicle Parks and Campgrounds;
      8.   Buildings And Facilities Accessible To The Handicapped: The 2009
version of the American Standard Specifications for Making Buildings and
Facilities Accessible to, and Usable by, the Physically Handicapped, published
by the American National Standards Institute;
      9.   Fire Code: The 2018 version of the International Fire Code,
published by the Western Fire Chief’s Association and the International
Conference of Building Officials and National Fire Protection Association Code,
published by the National Fire Protection Association, together with all
amendments, additions, changes, modifications and appendices or successor codes
thereto;
      10.   Public Works Construction: The current version of the Idaho
Standards for Public Works Construction, together with any amendments, changes,
modifications, appendices or successor codes thereto;
      11.   Mechanical Code: The 2018 version of the International Mechanical
Code, published by the International Conference of Building Officials and the
International Association of Plumbing and Mechanical Officials.
The adopted versions of the foregoing International Building Codes and Idaho
standards shall be deemed superseded by successive versions of such codes as
they are adopted by the Idaho Building Code Board effective on the date any
such codes are made effective by the Idaho Building Code Board and as
authorized by Idaho Code.
The above codes are hereby adopted by Payette County to provide for the
regulations set forth herein and to provide for the issuance of permits and the
collection of fees therefor. Three (3) copies of said adopted codes shall be
kept on file in the Office of the County Clerk and are hereby made a part
hereof by reference in the same manner as though fully set forth in this
chapter, notwithstanding any existing conflicting section contained in this
Code, which by the adoption hereof is hereby repealed. (Ord. 2018-4, 3-26-2018)
   B.   Permit Fees: Fees to enforce the above set out sections shall be
established by resolution of the Board of County Commissioners. Existing fee
resolutions are adopted until such time as new resolutions may be adopted. The
Board shall establish a permit fee schedule which schedule shall reflect the
fees which are to be charged by the official responsible for charging those
fees. The fee schedule shall be kept on file in the Office of the County Clerk
and in the office of the building official or building inspector and shall be
made available to the public upon request. The building official shall or a
designee shall charge permit fees in accordance with the schedule created by a
resolution of the Board.
      1.   For statutory provision or adoption of Construction Codes by
reference, see Idaho Code section 31-715.
      2.   For statutory provision on the State Building Codes and the
requirement that local governments comply with them, see Idaho Code section 39-
4116.
   C.   Building Permit Required: Any person who shall build or commence
construction of any building or structure without first obtaining a building
permit shall be subject to and shall pay a civil penalty in an amount equal to
twice the cost of the permit fee. This fee shall be paid before a permit is
issued.
   D.   Penalty:
      1.   A violation of this section shall be a misdemeanor punishable in
accordance with the general misdemeanor Statutes of the State of Idaho.
      2.   In addition, any building or other structure which is erected or
commenced in violation of this chapter, or in violation of the codes adopted in
subsection A of this section, in addition to subjecting the owner or builder to
misdemeanor penalties, shall be subject to nuisance or abatement procedures,
which may be brought by any County official, any member of the Planning and
Zoning Commission, the Planning and Zoning Administrator, building official,
building inspector or any other person.
      3.   In the event that any abatement procedure is successfully brought,
the person building said structure or the owner of the property upon which the
structure was wrongfully erected or commenced shall pay all court costs and
attorney fees for the prosecution of that action.
      4.   A violation hereof shall be a basis to revoke an existing permit and
shall be a basis for a civil abatement action. (Ord. 2014-01, 5-12-2014; amd.
Ord. 2020-03, 12-28-2020)
7-1-2: SUBSTANDARD ROADS, BUILDING PERMITS RESTRICTED:
   A.   Limitations Imposed:
      1.   Number Of Dwellings Or Structures: Any area which is served by a
single, substandard road, which road terminates in a cul-de-sac or in a dead
end, shall have no more than four (4) single-family or multiple-family
dwellings or commercial structures.
      2.   Private Driveway: A private driveway shall not serve more than two
(2) single-family or two (2) multiple-family dwellings.
      3.   Upgrade To Current Standards: After four (4) single-family or
multiple-family dwellings or commercial structures exist along any substandard
roadway as described in this subsection A, there shall be no additional
building permits available to the area served by the road unless and until the
roadway serving the area is brought up to then existing current County right-
of-way and design standards and the roadway is accepted by the Board of County
Commissioners.
      4.   Exceptions: This section does not apply to preexisting platted,
dedicated subdivisions which have been accepted by the Board of County
Commissioners.
   B.   Definition: A "substandard road" shall be defined as a roadway which
does not meet current right-of-way and design standards in existence at the
time an application for a building permit is made and which serves more than
one property owner and which has not been accepted for maintenance by the
County or Highway District 1. (Ord. 98, 6-19-1995)
7-1-3: ZONING CERTIFICATE REQUIRED FOR UTILITIES:
   A.   Definitions: As used in this section, the following words and terms
shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection:
   SERVICE: Providing, attaching or hooking up to any building, mobile home or
other structure any line or pipe, which line or pipe is intended to provide any
of the following services: telephone, gas, electricity, water or sewage
disposal.
   UTILITY: Any public or private corporation or company which supplies the
public or a group of individuals with the following commodity, service or both:
telephone, gas, electricity, water, or sewage disposal.
   ZONING CERTIFICATE: A certificate issued subject to the regulations as
described in title 8 of this code. (Ord. 23, 7-15-1974, eff. 7-18-1974)
!DEFEND!
   B.   Providing Service Without Certificate Prohibited: It shall be unlawful
for any utility, general contractor, or private property owner to install or
provide any service to any proposed building, mobile home or other structure
outside the limits of any incorporated city in the county until such utility,
general contractor, or private property owner has been furnished with a copy of
the zoning certificate which has been issued for such building, mobile home or
other proposed structure. (Ord. 23-A, eff. 11-24-1975)
   C.   Issuance Of Copies: When a zoning certificate is issued pursuant to
title 8 of this code, the issuer shall furnish to the successful applicant
copies in an amount sufficient for said successful applicant to furnish all
utilities with a copy.
   D.   Procedure On Violations: The procedure on violations of this section
shall be that procedure set out in title 8 of this code; however, said remedies
shall not exclude any other remedies herein or otherwise provided.
   E.   Penalty: Each violation of this section shall be a misdemeanor and
shall be punishable as provided in section 1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 23, 7-15-
1974, eff. 7-18-1974; amd. 1996 Code)
7-1-4: REBAR REQUIREMENTS:
On any construction, where nonengineered conventional concrete footings or
foundations are poured, in addition to any other requirement imposed by the
Payette County code or that part of the most recently adopted version of the
IBC, the following requirements shall apply: There shall be two (2) pieces of
#4 rebar horizontally embedded the entire distance of the footings. There shall
be two (2) pieces of #4 rebar horizontally embedded the entire distance of the
foundation. Each piece of rebar lying horizontally shall overlap twelve inches
(12") and shall be tied to the adjoining piece of rebar at the ends. One of the
two (2) pieces of the horizontal rebar in the foundation shall be placed
approximately six inches (6") from the top of the pour and the other piece of
horizontal rebar shall be placed approximately three inches (3") from the
bottom of the pour. There shall be one piece of #4 rebar embedded vertically on
six foot (6') centers the entire length of the foundation. The vertical rebar
in the foundation shall be tied to the horizontal rebar in the foundation. The
requirement of placement of rebar shall apply in all footings and foundations
which are poured along the perimeter of any structure or which are poured to
support interior walls or exterior projections. (Ord. 2000-6, 5-8-2000)

HOUSING, MANUFACTURED HOUSING, MODULAR HOMES AND MOBILE HOMES

State and shall have a date of manufacture after June 15, 1976. (Ord. 93, 1-9-
1995)

Building Code requirements, all State electrical codes and all State plumbing
codes. (Ord. 93, 1-9-1995)

CHAPTER 3
SIGN CODE
SECTION:
7-3-1: Title
7-3-2: Purpose
7-3-3: Authority
7-3-4: Applicability
7-3-5: Definitions And Abbreviations
7-3-6: Governmental Signs Excluded
7-3-7: Design And Construction Standards
7-3-8: Permit Required; Fees
7-3-9: Violation And Penalties
7-3-10: Nonaccessory Or Off Premises Signs
7-3-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and cited as the SIGN CODE. (Ord. 30, 9-26-1977,
eff. 9-29-1977)
7-3-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to provide minimum standards to safeguard life,
health, property and public welfare by regulation and controlling the design,
quality of materials, construction, location, electrification, and maintenance
of all signs and sign structures not located within a building. No sign shall
be erected in such a manner as to confuse or obstruct the view or
interpretation of any official traffic sign or device. The regulations of this
chapter are not intended to permit any violation of the provisions of any other
lawful ordinance. (Ord. 30, 9-26-1977, eff. 9-29-1977)
7-3-3: AUTHORITY:
These regulations are authorized by Idaho Code and article 12, section 2 of the
Idaho constitution. (Ord. 30, 9-26-1977, eff. 9-29-1977)
7-3-4: APPLICABILITY:
The regulations contained in this chapter apply to all signs and all use
districts described in title 8 of this code. (Ord. 30, 9-26-1977, eff. 9-29-
1977)
7-3-5: DEFINITIONS AND ABBREVIATIONS:
   A.   Purpose: For the purpose of this chapter, certain abbreviations, terms,
phrases, words and their derivations shall be construed as specified in this
chapter. Words used in the singular include the plural, and the plural the
singular. Words used in the masculine gender include the feminine, and the
feminine the masculine.
   B.   Definitions: As used in this chapter, the following words and terms
shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection:
   ANIMATED SIGN: A sign with action or motion, flashing color changes
requiring electrical energy, electronic or manufactured sources of supply, but
not including wind actuated elements such as flags, banners, or specialty
items. This definition does not include public service signs such as time and
temperature units.
   APPROVED PLASTIC MATERIALS: Those which have a flame spread rating of two
hundred twenty five (225) or less when tested in accordance with UBC standard
no. 42-1, in the way intended for use; and a smoke density rating no greater
than four hundred fifty (450) when tested in accordance with UBC standard no.
42-1, in the way intended for use; or a smoke density rating not greater than
seventy five (75) when tested in the thickness intended for use by the chamber
method of test under UBC standard no. 52-2.
The products of combustion shall be no more toxic than those of untreated wood
when burning under similar conditions.
   ARCHITECTURAL PROJECTION: Any projection which is not intended for occupancy
and which extends beyond the face of an exterior wall of a building, but shall
not include signs.
   BACKGROUND AREA OF SIGN: The entire background area of a sign upon which
copy could be placed. In computing area of sign background, only that face or
faces which can be seen from any one direction at one time shall be counted.
   BUILDING FACADE: That portion of any exterior elevation of a building
extending from grade to the top of the parapet wall or eaves and the entire
width of the building elevation.
   BUILDING FACADE FACING: A resurfacing of an existing facade with approved
material illuminated or nonilluminated.
   BUILDING OFFICIAL: The officer or other person charged with the
administration and enforcement of this Chapter or his duly authorized deputy.
   CHANGEABLE COPY PANEL: A panel which is characterized by changeable copy,
regardless of method of attachment.
   COMBINATION SIGN: Any sign incorporating any combination of the features of
pole, projecting, and roof signs.
   COPY AREA OF SIGN: The actual area of the sign copy applied to any
background. Compute copy area by straight lines drawn closest to copy
extremities encompassing individual letters or words.
   CURB LINE: The line at the face of the curb nearest to the street or
roadway. In the absence of a curb, the curb line shall be established by the
County Engineer. See Legal Setback Line.
   DIRECTIONAL SIGNS: On-premises incidental signs designed to guide or direct
pedestrians or vehicular traffic.
   DISPLAY SURFACE: The area made available by the sign structure for the
purpose of displaying the advertising message.
   ELECTRIC SIGN: Any sign containing electrical wiring, but not including
signs illuminated by an exterior light source.
   FIN SIGN: A sign which is supported wholly by a one-story building of an
open-air business or by poles placed in the ground, or partly by such a pole or
poles and partly by a building or structure.
   FREESTANDING SIGN: A sign which is supported by one or more columns,
uprights or braces in or upon the ground.
   GROUND SIGN: A billboard or similar type of sign which is supported by one
or more uprights, poles, or braces in or upon the ground other than a
"combination sign", "fin sign" or "pole sign", as defined by this Section.
   ILLUMINATED SIGN: A sign in which a source of light is used in order to make
the message readable. The definition shall include internally and externally
lighted signs.
   LEGAL SETBACK LINE 1 : A line established by ordinance beyond which no
building may be built. A legal setback line may be a property line.
   MARQUEE: Marquee is a permanent roofed structure attached to and supported
by the building and projecting over public property.
   MARQUEE SIGN: Any sign attached to or constructed in a marquee.
   MULTIPLE COPY SIGN: A sign which advertises other than the name of the
business and the principal product or service. Secondary copy not to exceed
fifty percent (50%) of display area.
   NONCOMBUSTIBLE: As applied to building construction material means a
material which, in the form in which it is used, is either one of the
following:
      1.   Material of which no part will ignite and burn when subjected to
fire. Any material conforming to UBC Standard No. 42-1 shall be considered
noncombustible within the meaning of this definition.
      2.   Material having a structural base of noncombustible material as
defined in subsection 1 of this definition, with a surfacing material not over
one-eighth inch (1/8") thick which has a flame-spread rating of fifty (50) or
less.
Noncombustible does not apply to surface finish materials. Material required to
be noncombustible for reduced clearances to flues, heating appliances, or other
materials shall refer to material conforming to subsection A of this
definition. No material shall be classed as noncombustible which is subject to
increase in combustibility or flame-spread rating beyond the limits herein
established, through the effects of age, moisture or other atmospheric
condition. Flame-spread rating as used herein refers to rating obtained
according to tests conducted as specified in UBC Standard No. 42-1.
   NONSTRUCTURAL TRIM: The molding, battens, caps, nailing strips, latticing,
cutouts or letters and walkways which are attached to the sign structure.
   OFF-PREMISES DIRECTIONAL SIGN: A sign mounted on property other than that
occupied by the business. This sign is regulated by the property frontage or
building on which it is supported.
   ON-PREMISES SIGN: A sign which carries only advertisements strictly
incidental to a lawful use of the premises on which it is located, including
signs or sign devices indicating the business transacted, services rendered,
goods sold or produced on the premises, name of the business, name of the
person, firm or corporation occupying the premises.
   PAINTED BULLETIN: Maximum size six hundred (600) square feet. A metal panel
with permanent painted copy. May be directional or advertising copy.
Freestanding signs to have unbraced supports and be landscaped when possible.
   POLE SIGN: A sign wholly supported by a sign structure in the ground.
   PORTABLE DISPLAY SURFACE: A display surface temporarily affixed to a
