   J.   Water Structures: Location, size and grade of water distribution
systems, pipes, valves and hydrants.
   K.   Land Use: The land use and existing zoning of the proposed subdivision
and the adjacent tracts.
   L.   Streets: Any existing or proposed streets, street names, rights of way
and roadway widths including adjoining streets or roadways.
   M.   Lot Information: Lot lines, dimensions and numbers, setback lines and
the total number of lots by block.
   N.   Topography: Land contours and grades.
   O.   Site Report: A site report as described in the rules of the Southwest
health district, percolation test results and water table data.
   P.   Utilities: Any proposed or existing utilities including, but not
limited to, storm and sanitary sewers, bridges, culverts, water mains, fire
hydrants, and their respective profiles or indicated alternative methods.
   Q.   Restrictions: Six (6) copies of any proposed restrictive covenants and/
or deed restrictions or, if none, a statement that none are proposed.
   R.   Existing Structures: Any existing structures, watercourses, railroad
lines and municipal boundary line.
   S.   Improvements: Curbs, gutters, sewers, sidewalks.
   T.   Public Dedications; Easements: Any dedications to the public and/or
easements, together with a statement of location, dimensions, and purpose of
such.
   U.   City Recommendation: Recommendation from any city in whose impact area
the subdivision will be.
   V.   Variances: A statement as to whether or not any variances will be
requested, and the reasons therefor.
   W.   Additional Information: All matters described in section 9-4-3 of this
chapter.
   X.   Technical Review Response: Discussion of compliance or defense of
noncompliance with technical review committee recommendations. (Ord. 2009-04,
6-15-2009)
9-4-5: REVIEW, CONSIDERATION, APPROVAL:
   A.   Review By Planning And Zoning Commission:
      1.   Hearing; Publication Of Notice: If the preliminary plat is properly
submitted and meets all requirements, within sixty five (65) days of the
meeting at which the preliminary plat is submitted, the planning and zoning
commission shall hold a public hearing.
         a.   At least fifteen (15) days prior to the hearing, notice of the
time and place and a summary of the proposal shall be published in the official
newspaper or a paper of general circulation within the jurisdiction.
         b.   At least fifteen (15) days prior to the public hearing, the
planning and zoning administrator shall send notice of the hearing to the
following persons:
            (1)   County engineer.
            (2)   Southwest health district or its successor.
            (3)   Payette County assessor.
            (4)   Idaho Power Company or its successor.
            (5)   Appropriate law enforcement and fire protection agencies.
            (6)   Any affected highway department.
            (7)   The telephone company providing local service to the affected
location.
            (8)   Department of water resources.
            (9)   Any drainage district in which the property may be located.
            (10)   Any water or irrigation district in which the property may
be located.
            (11)   Any city which has extended its impact area to encompass the
affected area.
            (12)   Any person, agency or easement holder which the zoning
administrator may deem is an appropriate party to receive notice.
      2.   Planning And Zoning Commission Recommendation: In conjunction with
the public hearing the planning and zoning commission will review the
preliminary plat and do the following:
Within sixty five (65) days of the public hearing, the planning and zoning
commission will submit the plat to the board of county commissioners, together
with written recommendations to approve, deny, conditionally approve with
modifications or approve subject to conditions. Motions to approve or deny will
be in order. Any recommendation to deny any plat shall clearly specify the
reasons for such recommendation. If no action is taken by the commission within
the said sixty five (65) day period, and if no extension of said period has
been obtained, the preliminary plat shall be submitted to the board without
recommendation.
   B.   City Recommendation: If the proposed property lies within a city impact
area, the preliminary plat will be considered by the city and a recommendation
may be sent to the county.
   C.   Consideration Of The Board Of County Commissioners: Within sixty five
(65) days of the receipt of the preliminary plat from the planning and zoning
commission, the board of county commissioners will schedule a public hearing
with notice to be given as set forth above. Within sixty five (65) days of the
public hearing the board will consider the preliminary plat; provided, however,
that the board shall not reschedule a public hearing or consider approval,
denial or approval with conditions for any preliminary plat until it has
received the same from the planning and zoning commission, together with the
recommendations of the said commission with respect to said plat. Upon
consideration of said preliminary plat, the board will either approve,
disapprove or approve with conditions or approve subject to modifications,
stating, in writing, the reasons for any denial or any conditions or
modifications. Any approval or denial will be done in accordance with Idaho
Code section 67-6535. (Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-2009)
9-4-6: CONDITIONS AND DURATION OF PRELIMINARY PLAT APPROVAL:
Approval of any preliminary plat by the board of county commissioners shall
continue for a period of one year. If the final plat is not presented within
the one year period, approval shall terminate, be rendered without effect and a
new application must be submitted. Provided, however, the board may extend such
period for a period not to exceed ninety (90) days, if such extension is
applied for prior to expiration and granted in writing. Approval of such
preliminary plat shall not constitute or guarantee approval of the final plat
of the subdivision involved, but approval will not be withheld without cause.
Any variation from the preliminary plat, any fact that renders the proposed
subdivision hazardous or unsafe for future inhabitants, or any fact that would
make the subdivision an undue burden on Payette County taxpayers shall be
sufficient cause. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984; amd. 1996 Code)
9-4-7: PREAPPLICATION AND FINAL PLAT PROCEDURE:
The preapplication procedure and final plat procedures adopted by Payette
County in sections 8-6-4 and 8-6-6 of this code are hereby incorporated herein
by reference as if set out in full. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-4-8: FINAL PLAT REQUIREMENTS:
All proposed final plats submitted for approval hereunder shall:
   A.   Approved Preliminary Plat: Conform to the approved preliminary plat and
meet any requirements or conditions thereof.
   B.   Subdivision Title: Conform to all requirements and provisions of this
title.
   C.   State Law: Conform to all requirements of Idaho law.
   D.   Drawing Specifications: Be drawn as provided by state law, Idaho Code
sections 50-1301 through 50-1306. The plat, diagram or drawing shall be drawn
at such scale and contain lettering of such size, including reference to
dedication and affidavit of survey, as to enable the same to be placed upon a
single sheet of paper with no part thereof nearer to the edge of said sheet
than one inch (1"). The reverse of the same shall not be used for any portion
of the drawing but may contain written matter as to dedication and other
information matters.
      1.   Preliminary control points, approved by the county engineer, or
description and "ties" to such control point, to which all dimensions, angles,
bearings, and similar data on the plat shall be referred. Such primary control
points must include either a section corner, quarter section corner or meander
corner according to government survey.
      2.   Tract boundary lines, right of way lines of streets, easements and
other right of way, and property lines of residential lots and other sites;
with accurate dimensions, bearings or deflection angles, and radii, arcs, and
center angles of all curves.
      3.   Name, centerline and right of way width of each street or other
right of way.
      4.   Location, dimensions and purpose of any easements.
      5.   Location and description of monuments.
      6.   Name and location of adjoining subdivisions.
      7.   Certification by surveyor and county engineer certifying to accuracy
of survey and plat.
      8.   Statement by owner dedicating street, rights of way and any sites
for public use.
      9.   Statement of dedication of easements.
      10.   Title, scale, north arrow, and date.
      11.   A provision setting forth the book, page and county recorder's fee
number where the protective covenants governing the subdivision are recorded
shall be noted and shown on the plat.
   E.   Required Signatures: The final plat shall be signed by the county
engineer charged with the responsibility of certifying to the correctness of
said plat, by such other persons as are required by law and also by the
chairman of the board of county commissioners.
      1.   The county shall designate a legally qualified, professional land
surveyor, one who is qualified to do land surveying in Idaho, to check the
sufficiency of any plat and the computations thereon, to determine that the
requirements of ordinances 40, 57 and any other applicable Payette County
ordinances and the Idaho Code are complied with. Said professional land
surveyor shall certify on the plat that the plat is in compliance with county
ordinances and state codes. For performing said service, the county shall
collect from any developer proposing a plat a fee which is adequate to cover
the cost of providing such service.
      2.   In the event the developer does not pay the fee in a timely manner
when billed, the county may file a lien against the land subject to the
subdivision request. In addition to filing a lien, the county may file a claim
against the developer in the form of a civil action.
      3.   For purposes of this section, an applicant, a subdivider or a
landowner shall be considered a developer.
   F.   Multiple Uses Indicated: Where more than one type of land use is
provided, sites to be used other than for one-family detached dwellings shall
be shaded or crosshatched and the purposes for which it is to be used
indicated. Where sites for one-family detached dwellings are not included, such
requirements shall apply to all uses other than the most substantial in area.
   G.   Setbacks: Minimum building setback lines on all lots and other sites
for front and side yards, on side street, and for rear.
   H.   Highway District Approval: In an area in the county where a county
highway district exists and is in operation, no plat shall be accepted for
recording by the county recorder, unless the acceptance of said plat by the
commissioners of the county highway district is endorsed thereon in writing, in
addition to the other endorsements required by statute or ordinance. (Ord.
2009-04, 6-15-2009)
9-4-9: FINAL PLATS, ADDITIONAL APPROVALS REQUIRED:
Prior to the submission of any final plat to the planning and zoning
administrator for approval in accordance with the provisions hereinafter
stated, the developer shall submit said final plat (and "as built" engineering
plans where required) to, and obtain approval of, the following authorities and
in the following order:
   A.   County engineer.
   B.   County surveyor.
   C.   The Southwest health district, or its successor.
   D.   The highway department.
   E.   The county assessor.
   F.   The county treasurer.
   G.   The county planning and zoning chairman.
   H.   Attest: The county clerk.
   I.   The chair of the county board of commissioners. (Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-
2009)
9-4-10: SUBMISSION OF FINAL COVENANTS AND RESTRICTIONS:
The developer shall submit to the planning and zoning administrator a statement
of covenants and/or restrictions. No more than one domicile, home or dwelling
unit shall be placed on any one parcel offered for sale or sold. (Ord. 2009-04,
6-15-2009)
9-4-11: BOARD OF COUNTY COMMISSIONERS REVIEW:
   A.   Review By Board Of County Commissioners: The board of county
commissioners shall review any submitted final plat, within thirty (30) days
after receipt of such final plat or at a meeting to be called within thirty
(30) days after such receipt; the board shall either approve or disapprove the
proposed final plat, and, if the same is disapproved, the board shall advise
the developer of such and state the reasons therefor in writing. The secretary
shall record all such proceedings in the minutes of such meetings, which
minutes shall be open to public inspection. Upon approval of any final plat by
the board, the chairman shall sign the required certificate of approval thereon
on behalf of the board. (Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-2009)
9-4-12: IMPROVEMENTS AND FACILITIES REQUIRED:
Prior to approval of any final plat, the board of county commissioners may:
   A.   Completion Of Improvements And Facilities: Require all improvements and
facilities to be completed.
   B.   Contract, Bond In Lieu Of Completion: In the event the board of county
commissioners does not require completion of all improvements and facilities,
the board shall require that the developer enter into a contract with the board
wherein such developer contracts that all such required improvements and
facilities will be completed pursuant to such contract; performance of any such
contract shall be guaranteed by a cash deposit, certified check, surety bond,
or irrevocable bank letter of credit in an amount sufficient to secure such
performance as determined by the board; provided, however, that the board shall
not require any bond duplicating any bond posted as required by another
governmental agency. Any security hereunder may be rebated or credited to the
account of the proprietor in proposition to the progress of the performance
secured thereby and as stated by written agreement between the board and the
developer. (Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-2009)
9-4-13: RECORDING OF FINAL PLAT:
No final plat shall be recorded until all prior steps have been taken, all
approvals required have been obtained, and all conditions imposed by the
planning and zoning commission or board of county commissioners have been
complied with. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-4-14: CONSTRUCTION STANDARDS:
Any construction in an approved subdivision shall be done in accordance with
the building codes 1  in effect at the time any building permit is requested.
(Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 7, chapter 1 of this code.
9-4-15: PAYMENT OF COSTS:
All engineering costs, including costs of review shall be borne by the
developer. Any costs levied or charged by county officials shall be paid by the
developer, and if not paid shall become a lien against said subdivision. (Ord.
2009-04, 6-15-2009)
9-4-16: REVERSION OF REZONED LANDS:
Section
8-5-8 of this code is incorporated herein as if set out in full verbatim and
adopted in full by reference. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
CHAPTER 5
RESERVED
(Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-2009)
CHAPTER 6
DESIGN STANDARDS
SECTION:
9-6-1: Minimum Design Standards
9-6-2: Street And Road Dedications
9-6-3: Street And Road Location
9-6-4: Street And Road Specifications
9-6-5: Parking
9-6-6: Street Names
9-6-7: Intersections
9-6-8: Pedestrian Walkways
9-6-9: Easements
9-6-10: Blocks
9-6-11: Crosswalks
9-6-12: Lots
9-6-13: Public Sites And Open Spaces
9-6-14: Commercial Or Industrial Modification
9-6-15: Unimproved Residential
9-6-16: Neighborhood Mailboxes
9-6-1: MINIMUM DESIGN STANDARDS:
All plats submitted pursuant to the provisions of this title, and all
subdivisions, improvements and facilities done, made or constructed, shall
fully comply with the minimum design standards set forth in this chapter;
provided, however, that any higher standards adopted by any highway district
shall prevail over those set forth herein. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-6-2: STREET AND ROAD DEDICATIONS:
Arterial streets shall be dedicated to the public in all cases; in general, all
other streets shall also be dedicated to public use. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-6-3: STREET AND ROAD LOCATION:
Street and road location shall conform to the following:
   A.   County Road Specifications 1 : All streets shall be designed in
compliance with the county road specifications which are set out in Payette
County road specifications or highway district 1 standards and regulations, as
amended; ordinance 40, as amended; or this code, as amended.
   B.   Local Or Minor Streets: Local or minor streets shall be so arranged as
to discourage their use by through traffic.
   C.   Existing Streets: The arrangement of streets shall provide for the
continuation of existing streets from adjoining areas into new subdivisions
unless otherwise approved by the board of county commissioners and the highway
district or department having jurisdiction over such streets.
   D.   Adjoining Areas Unsubdivided: Where adjoining areas are not subdivided,
the arrangement of streets in new subdivisions shall be such that said streets
extend to the boundary line of the tract to make provisions for the future
projection of said streets into adjacent areas.
   E.   Topography: Streets shall be arranged in proper relation to topography
so as to result in usable lots, safe streets and reasonable grades.
   F.   Alleys: Alleys shall not be permitted in areas of detached single- or
two-family residences; alleys shall be provided in multiple dwelling or
commercial subdivisions unless other provisions are made for service access,
off street loading and parking. Dead end alleys shall be prohibited in all
cases.
   G.   Arterial Street: Where a subdivision abuts or contains an arterial
street, it shall be required that there be frontage roads approximately
parallel with and on each side of the right of way of such arterial street, and
that there be such other treatment as is necessary for the adequate protection
of residential properties and to separate through traffic from local traffic.
Subdivisions shall be designed so that all traffic enters an arterial street, a
state highway or a county road from a single access point.
   H.   Cul-De-Sacs: Cul-de-sacs shall not be more than five hundred feet
(500') in length and shall terminate with an adequate turnaround having a
minimum radius of sixty feet (60') for right of way, exclusive of parking. Cul-
de-sacs are limited to residential subdivisions serving single-family dwellings
only.
   I.   Half Streets: Half streets shall be prohibited except where unusual
circumstances make such necessary to the reasonable development of a tract in
conformance with this title and where satisfactory assurance for dedication of
the remaining part of the street is provided. Whenever a tract to be subdivided
borders on an existing half or partial street, the other part of the street
shall be dedicated within such tract.
   J.   Private Streets And Roads: Private streets and roads shall be
prohibited. (Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-2009)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section 6-2-2 of this code.
9-6-4: STREET AND ROAD SPECIFICATIONS:
   A.   Street Right Of Way Width: Street and road right of way widths shall
conform to the adopted arterial plan and the rules of the state department of
highways and the highway district or department having jurisdiction. Minimum
right of way standards are as follows:
 
Street Types     Widths
Collector street 60 feet
Local street     60 feet
Major arterial   120 feet
Minor arterial   80 feet
 
   B.   Street Grades: Street grades shall not exceed nine percent (9%) on
either local or collector streets, and no street grade shall be less than one-
half of one percent (0.5%). To avoid the need for sanding, it is recommended
that street grades do not exceed five percent (5%).
   C.   Street Alignment:
      1.   Horizontal Alignment: When street lines deflect from each other by
more than ten degrees (10°) in alignment, the centerlines shall be connected by
a curve having a minimum radius of five hundred feet (500') for arterial
streets, and one hundred fifty feet (150') for local or minor streets. Between
reverse curve on minor streets, there shall be a minimum tangent distance of
one hundred feet (100'), and, on collector and arterial streets, two hundred
feet (200').
      2.   Vertical Alignment: Minimum sight distance shall be two hundred feet
(200') for minor streets and three hundred feet (300') for collector and other
streets. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-6-5: PARKING:
All dwellings and apartment houses shall provide parking space off the road or
street and outside the public right of way, together with the means of ingress
and egress thereto, for not less than two (2) motor vehicles per dwelling unit
or apartment. Each off street parking space shall not be less than ten feet
(10') wide and not less than twenty feet (20') long, shall be accessible from a
street or road, shall be properly drained and surfaced with gravel, asphalt,
concrete or equivalent material and shall be located within convenient walking
distance of the principal buildings for which the parking or loading space is
required. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-6-6: STREET NAMES:
The naming of streets shall be subject to review and shall conform to the
following:
   A.   Duplication Of Names: Street names shall not duplicate any existing
street name within Payette County except where a new street is a continuation
of an existing street; street names that may be spelled differently but sound
the same as existing streets shall not be used.
   B.   Rules For Naming: All new streets shall be named as follows: Streets
having a predominantly north-south direction shall be named "avenue" or "road",
streets having a predominately east-west direction shall be a numbered street
or "highway"; meandering streets shall be named "drive", "lane", "path",
"trail", "place", or shall conform to local customs. (Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-2009)
9-6-7: INTERSECTIONS:
Intersections shall conform to the following:
   A.   Angle Of Intersection: Streets shall intersect at ninety degrees (90°)
or as closely thereto as possible, and, in no case, shall streets intersect at
less than eighty degrees (80°).
   B.   Sight Triangles: Minimum clear sight distance at all minor street
intersections shall permit vehicles to be visible to the driver of another
vehicle when each is one hundred twenty five feet (125') from the center of the
intersection.
   C.   Number Of Streets: No more than two (2) streets shall cross at any one
intersection.
   D.   T Intersections: Except on arterials and certain collectors, T-type
intersections shall be used where practical.
   E.   Centerline Offsets: Slight jogs at intersections shall be prohibited;
where jogs are unavoidable, street centerlines shall be offset by a distance of
at least one hundred twenty five feet (125').
   F.   Vertical Alignment Of Intersections: An almost flat grade with
appropriate drainage slopes is desirable within intersections. This flat
section shall be extended fifty feet (50') to one hundred feet (100') each way
from the intersection. An allowance of two percent (2%) maximum intersection
grade in rolling terrain, and four percent (4%) in hilly terrain will be
permitted.
   G.   Minimum Standards: The board of county commissioners shall stipulate at
time of approval of each preliminary plat, the minimum standards of
construction. In no instance shall the dedicated streets have less than a sixty
foot (60') right of way, with usable width of thirty six feet (36') measured
from curb to curb. Requirements for construction shall meet or exceed the
requirements set up by the "highway department" as defined in section 9-2-2 of
this title. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-6-8: PEDESTRIAN WALKWAYS:
Right of way for pedestrian walkways in the middle of long blocks shall be
required where necessary to obtain convenient pedestrian circulation to
schools, parks or shopping areas; the right of way shall be at least ten feet
(10') wide and shall extend entirely through the block. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-6-9: EASEMENTS:
Unobstructed easements shall be provided along rear lot lines for utilities and
also along side lot lines when necessary; total easement width shall be not
less than five feet (5') along any one lot line and shall not be less than ten
feet (10') where lots adjoin. Unobstructed drainageway easements shall be
provided as required by the planning and zoning commission and the board of
county commissioners. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-6-10: BLOCKS:
Every block shall be so designed as to provide two (2) tiers of lots, except
where lots back onto an arterial street, natural feature, or subdivision
boundary; blocks shall not be less than five hundred feet (500') long in all
cases. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-6-11: CROSSWALKS:
Pedestrian crosswalks, not less than ten feet (10') wide may be required where
deemed essential to provide circulation, or access to schools, playgrounds,
shopping centers, transportation, and other community facilities, and shall be
constructed in accordance with the standards and specifications prescribed in
the manual containing the road standards and specifications adopted by Payette
County. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-6-12: LOTS:
Lots shall conform to the following:
   A.   Zoning: The lot width, depth, and total area shall not be less than the
requirements of any applicable zoning ordinance except where outlots are
provided and permitted pursuant to authority granted hereunder.
   B.   Lot Lines: Side lot lines shall be essentially at right angles to
straight streets and shall conform to the radius of curved streets.
   C.   Width Related To Length: Narrow, deep lots shall be avoided. The depth
of any lot shall not exceed one and one-half (11/2) times the width of said lot
as measured at the building line, except where unusual topographical features
of the subdivision warrant a variance.
   D.   Corner Lots: Corner lots shall have sufficient extra width to permit
appropriate building setback from both streets or orientation to both streets.
Lots abutting a pedestrian midblock crosswalk shall be treated as corner lots.
   E.   Uninhabitable Areas: Land subject to flooding or which shall otherwise
be deemed to be uninhabitable shall not be platted for residential purposes or
for any other uses that may increase or create a danger to health, life, or
property or which may increase or create a flood hazard. Such land within a
subdivision shall be set aside for other uses such as parks or other open
space.
   F.   Backup Lots: Lots shall not back into such features as freeways,
arterial streets, shopping centers, or industrial properties, except where
there is a marginal access street, unless a secondary access is provided. Such
lots shall contain a landscaped easement along the rear at least twenty feet
(20') wide in addition to the utility easement to restrict access to the
arterial street to minimize noise and to protect outdoor living areas. Lots
extending through a block and having frontage on two (2) local streets shall be
prohibited.
   G.   Lot Frontage: All rectangular lots shall have at least seventy five
feet (75') of frontage upon a publicly dedicated street. Variances may be
permitted for approved planning community unit development.
   H.   Future Arrangements: Where parcels of land are subdivided into
unusually large lots (such as when large lots are required for septic tank
operations), the parcels shall be divided, where feasible, to allow for
resubdividing into smaller parcels in a logical fashion when central utilities
are provided. Lot arrangements shall allow for the ultimate extension of
adjacent streets through the middle of wide blocks. Wherever such future
subdividing or lot splitting is contemplated, after public hearing, the plan
thereof shall be approved by the planning and zoning commission prior to the
taking of such action.
   I.   Lot Division: The division of a lot in a recorded plat is prohibited,
unless approved following application, review, and recommendation by the
commission and approval by the board of county commissioners. The application
shall be filed with the administrator and shall state the reasons of the
proposed division. No lot in a recorded plat shall be smaller in area than
permitted by title 8 of this code. No building permit shall be issued, or any
building commenced until the division has been approved by the board of county
commissioners and the suitability of the land for building sites has been
approved by the Southwest health district, or its successor.
   J.   Number Of Units Per Lot: No more than one single-family domicile, home
or dwelling unit shall be placed on any lot sold or offered for sale. (Ord.
2009-04, 6-15-2009)
9-6-13: PUBLIC SITES AND OPEN SPACES:
Public sites and open spaces shall conform to the following:
   A.   Public Uses: Where a proposed park, playground, school or other public
use shown on the comprehensive plan is located in whole or in part within a
subdivision, a suitable area for this purpose shall be dedicated to the public
or reserved for public purchase.
   B.   Natural Features: Existing natural features which add value to
residential development and enhance the attractiveness of the community (such
as trees, watercourses, historic spots, and similar irreplaceable assets) shall
be preserved, insofar as possible, in the design of the subdivision. (Ord. 40,
4-9-1984)
9-6-14: COMMERCIAL OR INDUSTRIAL MODIFICATION:
This title shall apply to the development of commercial subdivisions, except
that if there exists any discrepancy between the requirements of this title and
title 8 of this code, the requirements of title 8 of this code will prevail.
These subdivision design standards may be modified in accordance with section
9-4-1 of this title in the case of subdivisions exclusively for commercial or
industrial development, including shopping districts, wholesale areas, and
planned industrial districts. In all cases, however, adequate provisions shall
be made for off street parking and loading areas as well as for traffic
circulation. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-6-15: UNIMPROVED RESIDENTIAL:
The tax assessor shall regularly examine the records of the county. All lands
shall be classified and taxed accordingly. (Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-2009)
9-6-16: NEIGHBORHOOD MAILBOXES:
Any person who shall propose, build or create a new subdivision, a mobile home
park, a PUD which includes residential development, a residential development
consisting of six (6) or more dwelling units, or who expands an existing
subdivision, an existing mobile home park, or an existing PUD which includes
residential development, shall provide for the installation of consolidated
mailboxes, generally described by the United States postal service as a
neighborhood box unit (NBU) system. An NBU may also be known as a neighborhood
mailbox system, or a cluster box system. The NBU shall service homes within the
proposed development. (Ord. 1999-4, 9-13-1999; amd. Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-2009)
For developments of less than six (6) homes, a developer shall endeavor to
cooperate with adjoining landowners for the installation of an NBU system. Upon
application to the county planning and zoning administrator for a development
described herein, in addition to any other agencies entitled to notice, the
administrator shall notify the postmaster of the affected postal department of
the proposal. In addition, upon application to the county planning and zoning
administrator, after notice and public hearing, the requirement for an NBU
system in a development may be waived, for good cause shown. After construction
the developer shall create a homeowners' association which shall be responsible
to keep the system accessible to the postal carrier. (Ord. 1999-4, 9-13-1999)
CHAPTER 7
IMPROVEMENTS
SECTION:
9-7-1: Required Public Improvements
9-7-2: Optional Public Improvements
9-7-3: Guarantee Of Completion Of Required Improvements
9-7-1: REQUIRED PUBLIC IMPROVEMENTS:
Every developer shall be required to install the following public and other
improvements in accordance with the conditions and specifications as follows:
   A.   Monuments: Monuments shall be set in accordance with the Idaho state
code.
   B.   Streets And Alleys: All streets and alleys shall be constructed in
accordance with the standards and specifications adopted by the highway
department.
   C.   Curbs And Gutters: Curbs and gutters shall be required on neighborhood
access streets and/or roads that are dedicated in accordance to the standards
set by the "highway department" as defined in this title.
   D.   Installment Of Public Utilities: Public utilities and driveways shall
be located in accordance with the rules of the affected highway department.
Underground utilities will be required.
   E.   Driveways: All driveway openings in curbs shall be specified by the
highway department.
   F.   Storm Drainage: An adequate storm drainage system shall be required in
all subdivisions. The requirements for each particular subdivision shall be
established by the board of county commissioners. Construction shall follow the
specifications and procedures established by the board. All proposed storm
drainage construction plans for proposed plats shall be approved by the board.
   G.   Water Supply System: All proposed subdivisions, except those with less
than eight (8) lots, shall be served by a public water supply system; provided,
however, that the requirement may be waived if each of the proposed lots within
the subdivision consists of four (4) acres or more. The developer shall require
that all individual wells be constructed and drilled according to the
specifications for farm and rural dwellings, as required by the farmers home
administration of the U.S. department of agriculture.
   H.   Irrigation Water: If the parcel of land is subdivided and such parcel
has an irrigation water right by deed or certificate, then the developer shall
be required to deliver irrigation water to the corner of each lot with
sufficient pressure to serve that lot with sprinkler irrigation. A water users'
district shall be formed.
   I.   Irrigation Systems: No subdivision shall interfere with any existing
irrigation or drainage system. In the event any subdivision is constructed in
any area where irrigation ditches, canals or laterals or drainage works are
located, the developer shall ensure that no obstruction or structure is created
which will in any way interfere with the free flow of water. In the event any
subdivision is built around or bordering a ditch, canal, lateral or
drainageway, before filing of any final plat or before construction, the
developer shall first reach an agreement with the affected drainage or
irrigation district for proper tiling of any affected ditches or waterways. For
the protection of children all ditches shall be tiled before any occupancy
permits are issued for the entire subdivision.
   J.   Ditches, Laterals And Canals: All irrigation ditches, laterals or
canals, exclusive of natural waterways, intersecting, crossing or lying
adjacent and contiguous to an area being subdivided shall be covered, or if not
feasible, then fenced with an 11-gauge two inch (2") mesh chainlink fence or
other construction equivalent in ability to deter access to said ditch, lateral
or canal at least six feet (6') in height and securely fastened at its base at
all places where any part of said lands or areas being subdivided touch either
or both sides of said ditch, lateral or canal. Said fence shall not be cut,
gated or abridged. The commission may waive the requirements for covering or
fencing if it finds that the public purpose requiring such will not be served
in the individual case. Any covering or fencing program involving the
distribution system of any irrigation district shall have the prior approval of
the affected district. No subdivision plat shall be approved where the
subdivision is arbitrarily or artificially laid out to avoid being adjacent to
any irrigation ditch, lateral or canal to which it would otherwise be naturally
adjacent or which it would otherwise naturally include.
   K.   Sanitary Sewer System: When a proposed subdivision is to be serviced by
a public sanitary sewage system, sanitary sewers and other required
appurtenances thereto shall be provided by the developer. If there is no
existing or accessible public sewer system, a sewer system for the common use
of the lot owners may be required to be provided by the developer, if feasible,
in the judgment of the planning and zoning commission with the advice of the
Southwest health district. Where it is determined in the judgment of the
planning and zoning commission, with the advice of the Southwest health
district, that a subdivision cannot be economically connected with an existing
public or private sewer system or that a public or private sewer system cannot
be provided for the subdivision itself, then an approved disposal system may be
approved which shall comply with the requirements of the Southwest health
district.
   L.   Street Name Signs: Street name signs shall be installed in the
appropriate locations at each street intersection in accordance with the
requirements of the highway department.
   M.   Sidewalks And Pedestrian Walkways: Sidewalks may be required on both
sides of the street. Pedestrian walkways, when required, shall have easements
at least ten feet (10') in width and include a paved walk at least five feet
(5') in width, located generally along the centerline of the easement,
dedicated as a public pedestrian walkway. Sidewalks and crosswalks shall be
constructed in accordance with the requirements of the highway department.
   N.   Safety Requirements: The board of county commissioners may, upon its
own initiative, or upon the recommendation of the planning and zoning
commission, require that prior to the final approval of the proposed
subdivision, certain improvements be made in order to protect the public and
more particularly the occupants and residents of the subdivision from any
hazard or danger which may be present in or near the proposed subdivision.
   O.   Noxious Weeds: During the development period of any subdivision, a
developer shall not allow any noxious weeds to grow. To keep noxious weeds from
growing, a developer shall seed and maintain all cuts, fills and other open
areas with native grasses or some other grass seed approved by the board of
county commissioners. "Development period" shall be defined as the time between
the filing of an application for subdivision approval and the time the last
remaining lot is sold. In addition, the owner of any parcel in a subdivision
shall not allow any noxious weeds to grow thereon. "Noxious weeds" shall be
defined as any weed, plant or other vegetation which is defined as a noxious
weed by title 22, chapter 24 of the Idaho Code, the board of county
commissioners, or the United States of America, department of agriculture.
In the event the board of county commissioners, the county weed supervisor, the
county road supervisor, the county ordinance officer or any other designated
county employee is informed that noxious weeds are growing upon a person's
property, or are growing in an open area in a developing subdivision, a person
designated by the board of county commissioners shall notify the property
owner, the developer or a person responsible for the property, that noxious
weeds are growing thereon, and such growth is in a violation of this code. That
person shall also be notified that the weeds shall be destroyed within ten (10)
days of the notice. In the event the weeds are not destroyed within the ten
(10) day period, the county weed supervisor, county ordinance officer or any
other person designated by the board of county commissioners shall destroy the
weeds. All costs for weed eradication shall be charged to the property and
shall be collected as taxes are collected.
   P.   Acceptance: No subdivision, plat, road or other publicly dedicated
public improvement will be deemed accepted by the county until there is an
affirmative vote of the board of county commissioners. (Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-
2009)
9-7-2: OPTIONAL PUBLIC IMPROVEMENTS:
Optional public improvements shall be governed by the following:
   A.   Recreational: Where a school site, neighborhood park, recreation area,
or public access to water frontage is located in whole or in part in the
proposed subdivision, the board of county commissioners may request the
reservation of such open spaces for school, park and recreation or public
access purposes. All such areas shall be reserved either for the respective
school district, in the case of school sites, or for the county in all other
cases; however, voluntary dedication of these land areas will be accepted.
   B.   Greenbelts: Greenbelts may be required for the protection of
residential properties. Greenbelts or landscaped screen planting located
between a residential development and adjacent major arterial streets and
railroad rights of way may be required. Where a developer desires to protect
his development in this respect, a proposed subdivision plat shall show the
location of said greenbelts and provisions for maintenance.
   C.   Street Lighting: Streetlights may be required to be installed at
intersections throughout the subdivision. In these cases a developer shall
conform to the requirements of the county and the public utility providing such
lighting. (Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-2009)
9-7-3: GUARANTEE OF COMPLETION OF REQUIRED IMPROVEMENTS:
   A.   Financial Guarantee Arrangements; Exceptions: No lots or portions of
lots shall be sold or construction commenced until all public improvements are
installed. In lieu of the actual installation of public improvements, the board
of county commissioners, upon recommendation of the commission, may permit the
developer to provide a financial guarantee of performance for those
requirements which are over and beyond the requirements of the affected highway
department. The financial guarantee may be in the form of a surety bond, cash
deposit, certified check, negotiable bond or irrevocable bank letter of credit,
subdivision bond, completion bond or any combination thereof.
   B.   Surety Bond:
      1.   Accrual: The bond shall inure to the benefit of the county and shall
cover the costs of construction, operation, and maintenance of the specific
public improvement.
      2.   Amount: The bond shall be in an amount equal to the total estimated
costs of completing construction of the specific public improvement, including
contingencies, as determined by the board of county commissioners.
      3.   Term Length: The term length in which the bond is in force is until
improvements are in place.
      4.   Bonding Or Surety Company: The bond shall be with a surety company
authorized to do business in the state, acceptable to the board of county
commissioners.
      5.   Escrow Agreement: The escrow agreement shall be drawn and furnished
by the board of county commissioners.
   C.   Cash Deposit, Certified Check, Negotiable Bond, Or Irrevocable Bank
Letter Of Credit:
      1.   Treasurer, Escrow Agent Or Trust Company: A cash deposit, certified
check, negotiable bond, or an irrevocable bank letter of credit, such surety
acceptable by the board of county commissioners, shall accrue to the county.
These deposits shall be made with the county treasurer, or deposited with a
reputable escrow agent, or trust company, subject to the approval of the board
of county commissioners.
      2.   Dollar Value: The dollar value of the cash deposit, certified check,
negotiable bond, or an irrevocable bank letter of credit shall be equal to the
total estimated costs of construction of the specific public improvement
including contingencies, as estimated by a qualified engineering firm.
      3.   Escrow Time: The dollar value of the cash deposit, certified check,
negotiable bond, or an irrevocable bank letter of credit, shall be for a period
to be specified by the board of county commissioners.
      4.   Progressive Payments: In the case of cash deposits or certified
checks, an agreement between the county and the developer may provide for
progressive payments out of the cash deposit or reduction of the certified
check, negotiable bond or irrevocable bank letter of credit, to the extent of
the cost of the completed portion of the public improvement.
   D.   Conditional County Approval Of Final Plat: With respect to guarantees,
the approval of all final subdivision plats shall be conditioned on the
accomplishment of one of the following:
      1.   The construction of improvements required by this title shall have
been completed by the developer and formally accepted and approved in writing
at a regular meeting of the board of county commissioners.
      2.   Surety acceptable to the county shall have been filed in the form of
a cash deposit, certified check, negotiable bond, irrevocable bank letter of
credit or surety bond.
   E.   Inspection Of Public Improvements Under Construction: Before approving
final plat and construction plans and specifications for public improvements,
an agreement between the developer and the board of county commissioners shall
be made to provide for checking or inspecting the construction and its
conformity to the submitted plans.
   F.   Penalty In Case Of Failure To Complete The Construction Of A Public
Improvement: In the event the developer shall, for any reason, fail to complete
such work within the period of time as required by the conditions of the
guarantee for completion of public improvements, it shall be the responsibility
of the board of county commissioners to proceed to have such work completed. In
order to accomplish this, the board of county commissioners shall reimburse
itself for the cost and expense thereof by appropriating the cash deposit,
certified check, irrevocable bank letter of credit, subdivision bond,
completion bond or negotiable surety bond, or may take such steps as may be
necessary to require performance by the bonding or surety company, and as
included in a written agreement between the board of county commissioners and
the developer. (Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-2009)
CHAPTER 8
RESERVED
(Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-2009)
CHAPTER 9
HILLSIDE SUBDIVISIONS
SECTION:
9-9-1: Purpose
9-9-2: Appearance; Preservation
9-9-3: Applicability; Conflicts
9-9-4: General Requirements; Information
9-9-5: Hillside Development Evaluation
9-9-6: Engineering Plans
9-9-7: Grading Plan
9-9-8: Development Standards
9-9-9: Vegetation And Revegetation
9-9-10: Maintenance
9-9-11: Utilities
9-9-12: Request For Waiver
9-9-13: Inspection
9-9-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this Chapter is to identify various types of developments that
normally pose special concerns to the Planning and Zoning Commission and
elected officials when reviewing and acting upon subdivision requests. This
Chapter outlines the plan submittal requirements and design standards that
shall be taken into consideration when acting on special developments. The
provisions of this Chapter are in addition to the plan requirements, design
standards and improvement standards that are required by this Title 1 . (Ord.
40, 4-9-1984)
 
Notes
1 1. See Chapters 6 and 7 of this Title.
9-9-2: APPEARANCE; PRESERVATION:
In order to preserve, retain, enhance and promote the existing and future
appearance, natural topographic features, qualities and resources of hillsides,
special consideration shall given to the following:
   A.   Skyline and ridge tops;
   B.   Rolling grassy land forms, including knolls, ridges and meadows;
   C.   Tree and shrub masses, grasses, wild flowers and topsoil;
   D.   Rock outcroppings;
   E.   Stream beds, draws and drainage swales, especially where tree and plant
formations occur; and
   F.   Characteristic vistas and scenic panoramas. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-9-3: APPLICABILITY; CONFLICTS:
   A.   Scope: The provisions of this Chapter shall apply to any development
proposed for properties where any slope exceeds ten percent (10%), or where
adverse conditions associated with slope, stability, erosion or sedimentation
are present.
   B.   Conflicts: Wherever the regulations or standards contained in this
Chapter are in conflict with other Chapters of this Title or other pertinent
ordinances, the provisions of the more restrictive shall govern. (Ord. 40, 4-9-
1984)
9-9-4: GENERAL REQUIREMENTS; INFORMATION:
   A.   Project Engineer Required; Responsibilities: To ensure the necessary
coordination of manpower and technical data, the developer shall retain a
professional engineer registered in the State to serve as the project engineer.
It shall be the responsibility of the project engineer:
      1.   To prepare the grading plans;
      2.   To incorporate into the grading plans all recommendations contained
in the soils, geology and hydrology reports;
      3.   To inspect and certify all work within the project;
      4.   To act as coordinating agent if the need arises for liaison between
other professionals, the developer and the Planning and Zoning Commission; and
      5.   To prepare any revised plans and to submit to the Planning and
Zoning Commission record drawings of the plans upon the completion of the
project.
      6.   Prior to and during grading operations, all necessary reports,
compaction data, soils, geology and hydrology recommendations shall be
submitted by the project engineer to the Planning and Zoning Commission.
   B.   Report Substandard Work: If, in the course of fulfilling his
responsibilities, the project engineer discovers that the work is being
accomplished to a substantially lesser standard than required by this Title or
by the approved final grading plan, the discrepancy, if not corrected within a
reasonable time, shall be reported immediately, in writing, to the County
Engineer and to the Commission. Recommendations for corrective measures, if
applicable, shall be submitted.
   C.   Change In Key Personnel: If the project engineer, the soils engineer,
the geologist or the hydrologist of record is changed during the course of
work, the work shall be stopped until the replacement has agreed to accept the
responsibility for certification of the work within the areas of his technical
competence. In the event work stoppage is during inclement weather, protection
shall be provided for all open, vulnerable, unfinished work on the project,
including drainage. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-9-5: HILLSIDE DEVELOPMENT EVALUATION:
All development proposals shall take into account and shall be judged by the
way in which land use planning, soil mechanics, engineering geology, hydrology,
civil engineering, environmental and civic design, architectural and landscape
design are applied in hillside areas, including but not limited to:
   A.   Planning of development to fit the topography, soils, geology,
hydrology and other conditions existing on the proposed site;
   B.   Orientation of development on the site so that grading and other site
preparation is kept to an absolute minimum;
   C.   Shaping of essential grading to blend with natural land forms and to
minimize the necessity of padding and/or terracing of building sites;
   D.   Division of large tracts into smaller workable units on which
construction can be completed within one construction season so that large
areas are not left bare and exposed during the winter/spring runoff period;
   E.   Completion of paving as rapidly as possible after grading;
   F.   Allocation of areas not well suited for development because of soil,
geology or hydrology limitations for open space and recreation uses;
   G.   Minimizing disruption of existing plant and animal life; and
   H.   Consideration of the view from and of the hills.
Areas having soil, geology or hydrology hazards shall not be developed unless
it is shown that their limitations can be overcome; that hazard to life or
property will not exist; that the safety, use or stability of a public way or
drainage channel is not jeopardized; and that the natural environment is not
subjected to undue impact. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-9-6: ENGINEERING PLANS:
The developer shall retain a licensed professional engineer(s) to obtain the
following information, which information shall be submitted to the Planning and
Zoning Commission with the original application:
   A.   Soils Report: For any proposed hillside development a soils engineering
report shall be submitted with a preliminary plat. This report shall include
data regarding the natural distribution and strength of existing soils,
conclusions and recommendations for grading procedures, design criteria for
corrective measures, and opinions and recommendations covering the adequacy of
sites to be developed.
   B.   Geology Report: For any proposed hillside development a geology report
shall be submitted with the preliminary plat. This report shall include an
adequate description of site geology and an evaluation of the relationship
between the proposed development and the underlying geology and recommendations
of remedial remedies. The investigation and subsequent report shall be
completed by a professional geologist registered in the State. Any area in
which the investigation indicates geologic hazards shall not be subjected to
development unless the project engineer can demonstrate conclusively to the
Commission, based on the required engineering reports, that these hazards can
be overcome in such a manner as to prevent hazard to life or limb, hazard to
property, adverse effects on the safety, use or stability of a public way or
drainage channel, and adverse impact on the natural environment.
   C.   Hydrology Report: For any proposed hillside development a hydrology
report shall be submitted with the preliminary plat. This report shall include
an adequate description of the hydrology, conclusions and recommendations
regarding the effect of hydrologic conditions on the proposed development, and
opinions and recommendations covering the adequacy of sites to be developed.
Flood frequency curves shall be provided for the area proposed for development.
The investigation and subsequent report shall be completed by a professional
engineer registered in the State, and experienced and knowledgeable in the
science of hydrology and in the techniques of hydrologic investigation. Any
area in which the investigation indicates hydrologic hazards shall not be
subjected to development unless the project engineer can demonstrate
conclusively to the Commission based on the required engineering reports that
these hazards can be overcome in such a manner as to prevent hazard to life or
limb, hazard to property, adverse affects on the safety, use or stability of
the public way or drainage channel, and adverse impact on the natural
environment. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-9-7: GRADING PLAN:
   A.   Preliminary Grading Plan: A preliminary grading plan shall be submitted
with each hillside preliminary plat proposal. The grading plan shall be
designated to ensure that the lots within the development are able to conform
to the appendix, chapter 70, of the Uniform Building Code. The preliminary
grading plan shall include, but not be limited to, the following information:
      1.   Approximate limiting dimensions, elevations or finish contours to be
achieved by the grading, including all cut and fill slopes, proposed drainage
channels and related construction;
      2.   Preliminary plans and approximate locations of all surface and
subsurface drainage devices, walls, dams, sediment basins, storage reservoirs
and other protective devices to be constructed; and
      3.   A description of methods to be employed in disposing of soil and
other material that is removed from the grading site, including the location of
the disposal site.
      4.   All information required by this Title at the submission of the
preliminary plat;
      5.   Details and contours (2 foot intervals) of property;
      6.   Details of terrain and area drainage;
      7.   Location of any existing buildings or structures on the property
where the work is to be performed, the location of any existing buildings or
structures on land of adjacent owners which are within one hundred feet (100')
of the property or which may be affected by the proposed grading operations,
approximate locations of structures joining topography;
      8.   The direction of drainage flow and grade of all streets (not to be
requirement for final street design); and
      9.   Any and all other pertinent data.
   B.   Final Grading Plan: A final grading plan shall be submitted with each
final plat and shall include the following information:
      1.   All information required by this Title at the submission of the
preliminary plat;
      2.   Limiting dimensions, elevations or finish contours to be achieved by
the grading, including all proposed cut and fill slopes, and proposed drainage
channels and related construction;
      3.   Detailed plans and locations of all surface and subsurface drainage
devices, walls, dams, sediment basins, storage reservoirs and other protective
devices to be constructed; and
      4.   A schedule showing when each stage of the project will be completed,
including the total area of soil surface which is to be disturbed during each
stage together with estimated starting and completion dates. In no event shall
existing natural vegetative ground cover be destroyed, removed or disturbed
more than fifteen (15) days prior to grading.
   C.   Plan Preparation: The grading plan shall be prepared by a professional
engineer registered in the State who shall also serve as the overall project
engineer 1 ;
   D.   Modification Of Project Schedule: The Planning and Zoning Commission
may require that grading operations and/or project schedule be modified if
delays occur which result in weather-generated problems not anticipated at the
time approval was granted. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
 
Notes
1 1. See subsection 9-9-4A of this Chapter.
9-9-8: DEVELOPMENT STANDARDS:
   A.   Limiting Factors: Any area which presents one or more of the following
limiting factors shall not be subjected to development unless the project
engineer can demonstrate conclusively to the Planning and Zoning Commission,
based on the required engineering reports, that these limitations can be
overcome in such a manner as to prevent hazard to life, hazard to property,
adverse effects on the safety, use or stability of a public way or drainage
channel, and adverse impact on the natural environmental:
      1.   Landslide areas or scarps, or areas of active landslides;
      2.   Lines of active faults;
      3.   Soils with a high shrink/swell potential and hydrocompactable soils;
      4.   Soils with a unified classification of ML, CL, OL, MH, CH, OH and
PT;
      5.   Natural slopes greater than twenty five percent (25%);
      6.   Water table within six feet (6') of the surface at any time of the
year.
   B.   Soils:
      1.   Fill areas shall be prepared by removing organic material, such as
vegetation and rubbish, and any other material which is determined by the
engineer to be detrimental to proper compaction or otherwise not conducive to
stability; no rock or similar irreducible material with a maximum dimension
greater than eight inches (8") shall be used as fill material in fills that are
intended to provide structural strength.
      2.   Fills shall be compacted to at least ninety five percent (95%) of
maximum density, as determined by American Association of State Highway
Officials T99 (AASHO) and American Society for Testing Materials D698 (ASTM).
      3.   Cut slopes shall be no steeper than two horizontal to one vertical
(2:1); subsurface drainage shall be provided as necessary for stability.
      4.   Fill slopes shall be no steeper than two horizontal to one vertical
(2:1); fill slopes shall not be located on natural slopes two to one (2:1) or
steeper, or where fill slope toes out within twelve feet (12') horizontally of
the top of an existing or planned cut slope.
      5.   Tops and toes of cut and fill slopes shall be set back from property
boundaries a distance of three feet (3') plus one-fifth (1/5) of the height of
the cut or fill but need not exceed a horizontal distance of ten feet (10');
tops and toes of cut and fill slopes shall be set back from structures a
distance of six feet (6') plus one-fifth (1/5) the height of the cut or fill,
but need not exceed ten feet (10').
      6.   The maximum horizontal distance of disturbed soil surface shall not
exceed seventy five feet (75').
   C.   Roadways:
      1.   Road alignments should follow natural terrain and no unnecessary
cuts or fills shall be allowed in order to create additional lots or building
sites.
      2.   One-way streets shall be permitted and encouraged where appropriate
for the terrain and where public safety would not be jeopardized. Minimum width
shall be seventeen feet (17') between the backs of curbs.
      3.   The width of the graded section shall extend three feet (3') beyond
the curb back or edge of pavement on both the cut and fill sides of the
roadway. If sidewalk is to be installed parallel to the roadway, the graded
section shall be increased by the width of the sidewalk plus one foot (1')
beyond the curb back.
      4.   Standard six inch (6") vertical curb and gutter shall be installed
along both sides of all paved roadways.
      5.   A pedestrian walkway plan shall be required.
   D.   Driveways And Parking: Combinations of collective private driveways,
cluster parking areas and on-street parallel parking bays shall be used to
attempt to optimize the objectives of minimum soil disturbance, minimum
impervious cover, excellence of design and aesthetic sensitivity.
   E.   Grading And Stabilization: No grading, filling, clearing or excavation
of any kind shall be initiated until the final grading plan is formally
approved and a grading permit is obtained from the Planning and Zoning
Administrator/Building Inspector.
   F.   Retaining Walls Or Facings: All retaining walls or facings with a total
vertical projection in excess of three feet (3') shall be designed as
structural members keyed into stable foundations and capable of sustaining the
design loads.
   G.   Fill: Borrowing for fill shall be prohibited unless the material is
obtained from a cut permitted under an approved grading plan or imported from
outside the hillside areas of the County. No cuts shall be permitted solely for
the purpose of obtaining fill.
   H.   Stabilization: All disturbed soil surfaces shall be stabilized or
covered prior to December 1. If the planned impervious surfaces (e.g., roads,
driveways, etc.) cannot be established prior to December 1, a temporary
treatment adequate to prevent erosion shall be installed on those surfaces.
   I.   Hydrologic Controls: Interceptor ditches shall be established above all
cut/fill slopes, and the intercepted water conveyed to a stable channel or
natural drainageway with adequate capacity. Natural or improved open channel
drainageways shall be preserved or provided for in major waterways, except that
at road crossings, conduits may be permitted. Minor waterways shall be
permitted to be enclosed in conduits. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-9-9: VEGETATION AND REVEGETATION:
   A.   Slope Stabilization And Revegetation Plan: The developer shall submit a
slope stabilization and revegetation plan which shall include a complete
description of the existing vegetation, the vegetation to be removed and the
method of disposal, the vegetation to be planted, and slope stabilization
measures to be installed.
   B.   Contents Of Plan: The plan shall include an analysis of the
environmental effects of such operations, including the effects on slope
stability, soil erosion, water quality and fish and wildlife.
   C.   Vegetation: Vegetation sufficient to stabilize the soil shall be
established on all disturbed areas as each stage of grading is completed. Areas
contained within lot boundaries shall be protected with perennial vegetal cover
after all construction is completed. Efforts shall be made to plant those
species that tend to recover from fire damage and do not contribute to rapid
rate of fire spread.
   D.   Responsibility For Destroyed Vegetation: The developer shall be fully
responsible for any destruction of native vegetation proposed for retention. He
shall carry the responsibility both for his own employees and for all
subcontractors from the first day of construction until the notice of
completion is filed. The developer shall be responsible for replacing such
destroyed vegetation. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-9-10: MAINTENANCE:
The owner of any private property on which grading or other work has been
performed pursuant to a grading plan approved or a building permit granted
under the provisions of this Title shall continuously maintain and repair all
graded surfaces and erosion prevention devices, retaining walls, drainage
structures or means, and other protective devices, plantings and ground cover
installed or completed. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-9-11: UTILITIES:
All new service utilities shall be placed under ground. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-9-12: REQUEST FOR WAIVER:
Any developer who intends to request a waiver of any of the provisions of this
Chapter, must submit the request in writing. The request shall itemize each
requirement for which a waiver is sought and shall state the reason or reasons
for which each waiver is requested. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-9-13: INSPECTION:
   A.   Inspection And Testing: All construction subject to these regulations
shall be subject to inspection by the county engineer. When required by the
county engineer, special inspections and special testing shall be performed to
verify conformance with these regulations.
   B.   Costs: The costs of such special inspections and special testing shall
be borne by the developer.
   C.   Nonconformance: If such inspection determines that any portion of the
project is not in conformance with the requirements of this chapter and no
waiver of such requirements has been granted, the county engineer shall report
such discrepancy in writing to the project engineer within a specified period
of time not to exceed fifteen (15) days, and shall stop work on the project if
corrective action is not taken.
   D.   Stop Work Order: If any deficiency is deemed by the county engineer to
be an imminent threat to the public health, safety or welfare, he shall notify
the planning and zoning administrator, and the building inspector who will
require that work be stopped immediately until such deficiencies are corrected.
(Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-2009)
CHAPTER 10
PLANNED UNIT AND CONDOMINIUM SUBDIVISIONS
SECTION:
9-10-1: General Requirements
9-10-2: Minimum Area
9-10-3: Site Development Plan
9-10-4: Private Streets
9-10-5: Homeowners' Association
9-10-6: Storage Areas
9-10-7: Parking Spaces
9-10-8: Maintenance Building
9-10-9: Open Space
9-10-10: Control During Development
9-10-1: GENERAL REQUIREMENTS:
Planned units and condominium developments shall be subject to requirements set
forth in title 8 of this code and also subject to all provisions of this title.
(Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-10-2: MINIMUM AREA:
A planned unit development for the following principal uses shall contain an
area of not less than:
   A.   Three (3) acres or one city block for residential use;
   B.   Five (5) acres for residential use with subordinate commercial use;
   C.   Ten (10) acres for commercial use; and
   D.   Ten (10) acres for industrial use. (Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-2009)
9-10-3: SITE DEVELOPMENT PLAN:
The developer shall provide the planning and zoning commission with a colored
rendering of adequate scale to show the completed development that will include
at least the following:
   A.   Architectural style and building design;
   B.   Building materials and color;
   C.   Landscaping;
   D.   Screening;
   E.   Garbage areas;
   F.   Parking; and
   G.   Open space. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-10-4: PRIVATE STREETS:
Private street construction standards will conform to county road
specifications. Adequate construction standards may vary depending on the size
of the development and the demands placed on such improvements. (Ord. 40, 4-9-
1984)
9-10-5: HOMEOWNERS' ASSOCIATION:
The homeowners' association bylaws and other similar deed restrictions, which
provide for the control and maintenance of all common areas, recreation
facilities or open space, shall meet with the approval of the board of county
commissioners. Any and all powers as specified in such agreements may also be
assigned to the board for the purpose of assessing property for delinquencies
and enforcement of motor vehicle speed to protect the best interest of the
owners involved and the general public. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-10-6: STORAGE AREAS:
Storage areas shall be provided for the anticipated needs of boats, campers and
trailers. For typical residential development, one adequate space shall be
provided for every two (2) living units. This may be reduced by the board of
county commissioners if there is a showing that the needs of a particular
development are less. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-10-7: PARKING SPACES:
One additional parking space beyond that which is required by title 8 of this
code may be required for every three (3) dwelling units to accommodate visitor
parking. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-10-8: MAINTENANCE BUILDING:
A maintenance building shall be provided; size and location to be suitable for
the service needs that are necessary for the repair and maintenance of all
common areas. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-10-9: OPEN SPACE:
The location of open space shall be appropriate to the development and shall be
of such shape and area to be usable and convenient to the residents of the
development. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-10-10: CONTROL DURING DEVELOPMENT:
Single ownership or control during development shall be required, and a time
limit may be imposed to guarantee the development is built and constructed as
planned. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
CHAPTER 11
LARGE-SCALE DEVELOPMENT SUBDIVISIONS
SECTION:
9-11-1: Required Information
9-11-1: REQUIRED INFORMATION:
Due to the impact that a large-scale development would have on public utilities
and services, the developer shall submit the following information along with
the preliminary plat:
   A.   Identification of all public services that would be provided to the
development (i.e., fire protection, police protection, central water, central
sewer, road construction, parks and open space, recreation, maintenance,
schools and solid waste collection);
   B.   An estimate of the public service costs to provide adequate service to
the development;
   C.   An estimate of the tax revenue that will be generated from the
development; and
   D.   Suggested public means of financing the services for the development if
the cost for the public services would not be offset by tax revenue received
from the development. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
CHAPTER 12
SUBDIVISIONS WITHIN A FLOODPLAIN
SECTION:
9-12-1: Flood Areas
9-12-1: FLOOD AREAS:
There shall be no subdivisions upon any lands lying within a floodplain. (Ord.
2009-04, 6-15-2009)
CHAPTER 13
VARIANCES
SECTION:
9-13-1: General; Qualifications
9-13-2: Topographical Physical Limitation; Variances
9-13-3: Planned Unit Development
9-13-4: Application And Standards
9-13-5: Supplementary Conditions And Safeguards
9-13-6: Public Hearing
9-13-7: Action By The Planning And Zoning Commission
9-13-1: GENERAL; QUALIFICATIONS:
The planning and zoning commission may recommend to the board of county
commissioners a variance from the provisions of this title on a finding that
undue hardship may result from strict compliance with specific provisions or
requirements of this title or that application of such provision or requirement
is impracticable. The commission shall only recommend variances that it deems
necessary to or desirable for the public interest. In making its findings, as
required hereinbelow, the commission shall take into account the nature of the
proposed use of land and the existing use of land in the vicinity, the number
of persons to reside or work in the proposed subdivision, and the probable
effect of the proposed subdivision upon traffic conditions in the vicinity. No
variance shall be recommended unless the commission finds that there are
special conditions, such as:
   A.   That there are such special circumstances or conditions affecting said
property that the strict application of the provisions of this title would
clearly be impracticable or unreasonable. In such cases the developer shall
first state his reasons in writing as to the specific provisions or requirement
involved and submit them to the planning and zoning commission.
   B.   That the granting of the specified variance will not be detrimental to
the public welfare or injurious to other property in the area in which said
property is situated.
   C.   That such variance will not violate the provisions of the Idaho Code.
   D.   That such variance will not have the effect of nullifying the interest
and purpose of this title, title 8 of this code, and the comprehensive plan of
the county. (Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-2009)
9-13-2: TOPOGRAPHICAL PHYSICAL LIMITATION; VARIANCES:
Where, in the case of the particular proposed subdivision, it can be shown that
strict compliance with the requirements of this title would result in
extraordinary hardship to the developer because of unusual topography, other
physical conditions, or other such conditions which are not self-inflicted, or
that these conditions would result in inhibiting the achievement of the
objectives of this title, the commission may recommend to the board of county
commissioners that a variance modification or a waiver of these requirements be
granted. (Ord. 2009-04, 6-15-2009)
9-13-3: PLANNED UNIT DEVELOPMENT:
The developer may request a variance from specified portions of this title in
the case of planned unit development. If in the judgment of the planning and
zoning commission such a plan provides adequate public spaces and includes
provisions for efficient circulation, light and air and other needs, it shall
make findings, as required below. The commission shall take into account the
nature of the proposed use of the land and existing use of land in the
vicinity, the number of persons to reside or work in the proposed subdivision,
and the probable effect of the proposed subdivision upon traffic conditions in
the vicinity. The commission shall report to the board of county commissioners
whether:
   A.   The proposed project will constitute a desirable and stable community
development.
   B.   The proposed project will be in harmony with adjacent areas. (Ord. 40,
4-9-1984)
9-13-4: APPLICATION AND STANDARDS:
A variance from the terms of this title shall not be granted by the commission
unless and until a written application for a variance is submitted to the
planning and zoning administrator/building inspector and the planning and
zoning commission, which application contains the following information:
   A.   Name, address and phone number of applicant(s);
   B.   Legal description of property;
   C.   Description of nature of variance requested; and
   D.   Names and addresses of property owners within three hundred feet (300')
beyond the external boundaries of the land being considered;
   E.   A filing fee shall accompany the application;
   F.   A narrative statement demonstrating that the requested variance
conforms to the following standards:
      1.   That special conditions and circumstances exist which are peculiar
to the land, structure or building involved and which are not applicable to
other lands, structures or buildings in the zone;
      2.   That a literal interpretation of the provisions of this title would
deprive the applicant of rights commonly enjoyed by other properties in the
same zone under the terms of this code;
      3.   That special conditions and circumstances do not result from the
actions of the applicant; and
      4.   That granting the variance requested will not confer on the
applicant any special privilege that is denied by this title to other lands,
structures or buildings in the same zone. A variance attaches to the realty and
is transferable with the title to the property.
A variance shall not be granted unless the planning and zoning commission makes
specific findings of fact based directly on the particular evidence presented
to it which support conclusions that the above mentioned standards and
conditions have been met by the applicant. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984; amd. 1996 Code)
9-13-5: SUPPLEMENTARY CONDITIONS AND SAFEGUARDS:
Under no circumstances shall the planning and zoning commission grant a
variance to allow a use not permissible under the terms of this code in the
zone involved, or any use expressly or by implication prohibited by the terms
of this code in said zone. In granting any variance, the commission may
prescribe appropriate conditions and safeguards and, when made a part of the
terms under which the variance is granted, any deviation shall be deemed a
violation of this title. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984; amd. 1996 Code)
9-13-6: PUBLIC HEARING:
Upon receipt of the application for a variance, the planning and zoning
commission shall hold a public hearing, publish notice in a newspaper of
general circulation within the county, and give written notice to all parties
as required in section
8-11-6 of this code. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
9-13-7: ACTION BY THE PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION:
   A.   Decision Of Planning And Zoning Commission: Within sixty five (65) days
after the public hearing or at the next regular meeting of the planning and
zoning commission, whichever occurs last, the commission shall either approve,
conditionally approve or disapprove the request for a variance.
   B.   Grounds For Decision: Upon granting or denying an application, the
planning and zoning commission shall specify:
      1.   The ordinance and standards used in evaluating the application;
      2.   The reasons for approval or denial; and
      3.   The actions, if any, that the applicant could take to obtain a
permit.
   C.   Written Notice To Applicant: Within thirty (30) days after a decision
has been rendered, the planning and zoning administrator/building inspector
shall provide the applicant with written notice of the action on the request.
   D.   Appeal: The applicant or any affected person who appeared in person or
in writing before the planning and zoning commission may appeal the decision of
the commission to the board of county commissioners, in accordance with this
title. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
CHAPTER 14
AMENDMENT PROCEDURES
SECTION:
9-14-1: Amendment
9-14-1: AMENDMENT:
   A.   The Board of County Commissioners may, from time to time, amend,
supplement or repeal the regulations and provision of this Title in the manner
prescribed by the Idaho Code.
   B.   Notice and hearing provisions as set forth in Idaho Code section 67-
6509, will be followed.
   C.   A proposed amendment, supplement or repeal may be originated by the
Board of County Commissioners or Planning and Zoning Commission. All proposals
shall be reviewed by the Commission for their recommendations and a report
thereon before any action is taken on the proposal. Hearings shall be held by
the Commission before any changes are recommended. The Board will hold a public
hearing before any changes are made. (Ord. 40, 4-9-1984)
TITLE 10
AIRPORT HAZARD ZONING
CHAPTER 1
PAYETTE AIRPORT
SECTION:
10-1-1: Title
10-1-2: Purpose And Authority
10-1-3: Scope
10-1-4: Definitions
10-1-5: Airport Administrator
10-1-6: Zones Established
10-1-7: Land Use Safety Zones
10-1-8: Permits
